GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 50.01 BACKFLOW PREVENTION DEVICES.
   (A)   A cross-connection control officer shall be appointed by the Board of
Trustees of the village to oversee the enforcement of this section. This person
shall be responsible for reviewing the surveys submitted by the customers of
the Village Water Department and determining if a backflow prevention device is
required to comply with Title 179, NAC 2, “Regulations Governing Public Water
Supply Systems.” These regulations are incorporated by reference, the same as
those copied at length herein that are applicable to the village.
   (B)   All customers of the Village Water Department shall be required to
report to the cross-connection control officer any potential cross-connections
which may be on their premises. This report shall be made at least every five
years.
   (C)   (1)   A customer of the Village Water Department may be required by
the cross-connection control officer to install and maintain a properly located
backflow prevention device at the customer’s expense appropriate to the
potential hazard as set forth in Title 179, NAC 2, “Regulations Governing
Public Water Supply Systems” and approved by the cross-connection control
officer.
      (2)   The customer shall make application to the cross-connection control
officer to install a required backflow prevention device on a form provided by
the municipality. The application shall contain, at a minimum, the name and
address of the applicant, the type of backflow prevention device to be
installed, including make and model number, and the location of the proposed
installation.
      (3)   The cross-connection control officer shall approve or disapprove
the application based on whether such installation will protect the municipal
water distribution system from potential backflow and backsiphonage hazards.
      (4)   When a testable backflow prevention device shall be required, the
customer shall also certify to the municipality at least one time annually that
the backflow prevention device has been tested by a State Health and Human
Services System Grade VI certified water operator. Such certification shall be
made on a form available at the office of the Village Clerk.
      (5)   Any decision of the cross-connection control officer may be
appealed to the Board of Trustees of the village. The owner may file a written
notice of appeal with the Village Clerk within ten days after the decision of
the cross-connection control officer has been made. The Village Board of
Trustees shall hear all appeals and shall have the power and authority when
appealed to, to modify the decision or order of the cross-control officer. Such
decision shall be final, subject to any remedy, which the aggrieved party may
have at law or equity. Appeals shall be in writing and shall state the reason
for appeal.
   (D)   Any customer refusing to report on possible cross-connections on their
premises, refusing to install the necessary backflow prevention device, or
failing to have a testable backflow prevention device tested at least annually
shall be in violation of this subchapter and may have their water service
discontinued. Any customer who has had their service discontinued for violation
of this section shall be subject to a $100 reconnect fee to have the service
reinstated after supplying proof that the potential cross-connection has been
eliminated or properly protected.
(Ord. 346, passed 12-6-2005) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.02 WATER WELLS.
   (A)   For purposes of this section, WATER WELL shall mean any excavation
that is drilled, corralled, bored, washed, dug, driving, jetted, or otherwise
constructed for the purpose of exploring for ground water, monitoring ground
water, utilizing the geothermal property of the ground or extracting water from
or injecting water into the underground water. WATER WELL shall not include any
excavation made for obtaining or prospecting for oils, natural gas, mineral, or
products mined or quarried or inserting media to repressure oil or natural gas
bearing formation. The intent of this section is to establish control by the
village over the location of future potential sources of contamination within
the village and the extraterritorial jurisdiction of the village’s drinking
water system, so as to prevent or minimize any hazards to the safety of the
village’s drinking water.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful to place, construct, or replace any of the water
wells in the village limits except for the purpose of geothermal property of
ground through closed loop geothermal systems, which must be approved by
permit.
   (C)   The construction of a geothermal closed loop within the corporate
limits or construction of a water well within one mile of the corporate limits
of the village shall not be started unless a permit approved by the Village
Board.
   (D)   The village may consider permits to allow placement of water wells
within one mile of corporate limits and for closed loop geothermal wells as
under criteria defined by the state regulations governing public water supply
systems (Title 179, NAC2) and state regulations governing water well
construction, pump installation and water well abandonment standards (Title
178, NACI2), as amended from time to time. Placement shall be allowed only
under the following conditions:
      (1)   The village shall refer the application to its engineer for
evaluation and report. The estimated cost of the engineer’s fees must be paid
at the time of filing the application. Any additional costs which are
reasonably incurred by the engineer in making his or her examination and report
shall be paid by the applicant in addition to any previously paid estimated
costs.
      (2)   The Village Board shall consider the engineer’s report and any
additional information submitted by the applicant. In reaching its decision on
whether to allow the placement of a water well, as defined in division (A)
above, the village must act to prevent all sources of possible or likely water
contamination.
      (3)   If, in the opinion of the Village Board, the proposed use poses a
risk of contaminating a village water supply well, he or she shall deny the
permit. The applicant may appeal the decision of the Village Board by filing an
appeal with the Village Clerk within 30 days of the Village Board’s decision.
Appeal of the decision of the Village Board shall be to the District Court of
the county within 30 days of the Village Board’s decision.
      (4)   If the Village Board approves the installation, it shall submit the
application together with the engineer’s report to the State Department of
Health for a final approval or denial. No installation shall be made without
the approval of both the Village Board and the State Department of Health.
   (E)   Water wells in existence and use shall continue to be permitted unless
such continued existence or use presents a hazard to the quality of the
drinking water available for public use to the village. The owner of any water
well shall have the burden of establishing the existence and use of such well
at the time of the effective date of this section.
   (F)   It shall be unlawful for any wells that are governed by this section
to be discharged into the sewer system of the village.
(Ord. 360, passed 3-2-2010) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.03 FLUORIDE IN WATER SUPPLY.
   Fluoride shall not be added to the water supply of the village. If it is
desired that fluoride be added to the water supply of the village, a petition
may be made, and it shall be presented on the ballot so that the voters may
take initiative.
(Ord. 231A, passed 3-13-1974) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.04 WELLHEAD PROTECTION AREA.
   (A)   WELLHEAD PROTECTION AREA means the surface and subsurface area
surrounding a water well or well field, supplying a public water system,
through which contaminants are reasonably likely to move toward and reach such
water or well field.
   (B)   The Village Board designates a Wellhead Protection Area for the
purpose of protection of the public water system. The boundaries of the
Wellhead Protection Area are set forth and the delineation is based upon a map
prepared by the State Department of Environmental Quality or the State Rural
Water Association and presented to the village. This map shall become and is
incorporated into the terms of this section as if at full set forth herein, and
such map shall be further identified as the Wellhead Protection Area Map.
   (C)   In accordance with Title 179, Ch. 2, State Department of Health
Regulations Governing Public Water Supply Systems, the minimum horizontal
distance in feet separating a municipal water supply well of the village from
potential sources of contamination shall be as described below:
Category Distance
         Feet Meters
Category                                                        Distance
                                                                Feet  Meters
Absorption or disposal field for waste                          500   150
All water wells, including, but not limited to, domestic supply 1,000 300
wells, irrigation wells, stock wells, and heat pump wells
Chemical or petroleum product storage                           500   150
Cesspool                                                        500   150
Corral                                                          500   150
Dump                                                            500   150
Feedlot or feedlot runoff                                       500   150
Pit toilet                                                      500   150
Sanitary landfill                                               500   150
Sanitary sewer connection                                       100   30
Sanitary sewer line                                             50    15
Sanitary sewer line (permanently water-tight)                   10    3
Sanitary sewer manhole                                          100   30
Septic tank                                                     500   150
Sewage lagoon                                                   1,000 300
Sewage treatment plant                                          500   150
Sewage wet well                                                 500   150
   (D)   When, in the judgment of the village or the State Department of
Health, surface runoff or underground movement from potential sources of
contamination may adversely affect the quality of water in a municipal water
supply well, the distance separating these potential sources of contamination
and the well shall be greater than that listed in division (C) above.
   (E)   Any person desiring to erect a new potential contamination source or
enlarge an existing one shall file an application for a permit with the Village
Board, on a form furnished by the village for that purpose. After reviewing the
application, the Village Board shall approve or deny said permit. If, in the
opinion of the Village Board, the proposed use poses a risk of contamination of
a municipal water supply or well, the Board shall deny the permit. The
applicant may appeal the decision of the Village Board by filing an appeal with
the Village Clerk within 30 days of the Board’s decision. The Village Board
will then review the appeal and make a decision. If the appeal is denied, the
applicant shall have the ability to appeal the decision to the district court
of the county. Said appeal must be filed within 30 days of the Village Board’s
decision upon the prior appeal.
   (F)   The provisions of this section shall apply to all land within the
corporate limits of the village and that portion of the unincorporated area
within one mile of the corporate limits of the village.
   (G)   The provisions of this section shall supersede any land use regulation
which allows the installation of a potential contaminant source on a parcel of
land. Nothing in this section shall be construed to allow the installation of
any category of contamination source which is restricted or prohibited by any
federal, state, or local law statute, regulation, or ordinance.
(Ord. 295, passed - -; Ord. 334, passed 3-5-2002; Ord. 359, passed 3-2-2010)
Penalty, see §
50.99
WATER SYSTEM
§ 50.15 RULES AND REGULATIONS PART OF CONSUMER’S CONTRACT.
   The rules, regulations, and water rates hereinafter set out shall be
considered a part of the contract with every person who is now or hereafter
shall be supplied with water through the village, and every such consumer, by
taking water, shall be considered and held to consent to be bound thereby. When
any such rules and regulations now or hereafter adopted by said village, shall
be violated, the water shall be cut off from the building or place of
violation, and shall not be turned on again, except by order of the Utility
Superintendent, and on payment of the expense of shutting off and turning on
such water, and upon such other terms as the Village Board shall determine.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.16 APPLICATION FOR WATER SERVICE.
   Every person desiring a supply of water must contact the Village Office and
complete an application for the same. Each application by an owner or a renter
of the premises to be supplied shall be required to pay a $100 water deposit.
If application is made by a non-owner (renter) of the premises, the owner must
sign the application so that the services automatically transfer to the owner
when there is a disconnection, whether it be voluntary or non-voluntary by a
tenant.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021)
§ 50.17 TAP FEES.
   (A)   Tap fee within corporate limits. For each new water connection to
premises within the corporate limits, the tap fee shall be $25.
   (B)   Tap fee, outside corporate limits. For each new water connection to
premises outside the corporate limits, the tap fee shall be such amount as the
Utility Superintendent shall determine based on the cost of pipe and fittings.
   (C)   Tap fee; service rendered for. The village shall furnish the material
only to tap the commercial main. All other expenses to bring in water service
into and upon premises shall be borne by the applicant. The curb stop valve
shall be located eight feet inside the curb line. The applicant shall furnish a
freeze proof meter pit constructed in accordance with the specifications of the
Utility Superintendent, unless by agreement of the applicant and the Utility
Superintendent, the meter is placed in the basement of the premises.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021)
§ 50.18 SEPARATE TAP AND SUPPLY PIPE FOR EACH PREMISES SERVED.
   Not more than one separate premises shall be supplied from the same tap or
supply pipe without the permission of the Utility Superintendent.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.19 METER READING.
   The Utility Superintendent shall read or cause to be read every water meter
used in the village at such times as are necessary that the bills may be sent
out at the proper time.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021)
§ 50.20 WATER RATES.
   The Village Board shall set the rates to be charged for services rendered by
resolution, and shall file a copy of all resolutions establishing the rates
with the office of the Village Clerk for public inspection at any reasonable
time.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021)
§ 50.21 COLLECTION; NON-PAYMENT.
   (A)   All water bills are due on the billing date and are delinquent 30 days
after the billing of the water bill and shall be payable at the office of the
Village Clerk. If any bill is not paid within ten days after becoming
delinquent, a penalty of 10% shall be added thereto, and if ten days elapse and
said water bill and penalty are not paid, the water service of the consumer
shall be shut off and shall not be turned on again until said bill, penalty,
and other charges, if any, due the village shall be paid together with a fee of
$25 for resumption of service.
   (B)   Owners of premises are responsible for payment of past due water bills
left unpaid by renters of their premises.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.22 DISCONNECTION FOR LATE PAYMENT.
   (A)   It is the policy of the village to discontinue utility service to
customers by reason of nonpayment of bills only after notice and a meaningful
opportunity to be heard on disputed bills. The village’s form for application
for utility service and all bills shall contain, in addition to the title,
address, room number, and telephone number of the official in charge of
billing, clearly visible and easily readable provisions to the effect:
      (1)   That all bills are due and payable on or before the date set forth
on the bill;
      (2)   That if any bill is not paid by or before that date, a second bill
will be mailed containing a cutoff notice that if the bill is not paid within
ten days of the mailing of the second bill, service will be discontinued for
nonpayment; and
      (3)   That any customer disputing the correctness of his or her bill
shall have a right to a hearing at which time he or she may be represented in
person and by counsel or any other person of his or her choosing and may
present orally or in writing his or her complaint and contentions to the city
official in charge of utility billing. This official shall be authorized to
order that the customer’s service not be discontinued and shall have the
authority to make a final determination of the customer’s complaint.
   (B)   Requests for delays or waiver of payment will not be entertained; only
questions of proper and correct billing will be considered. In the absence of
payment of the bill rendered or resort to the hearing procedure provided
herein, service will be discontinued at the time specified, but in no event
until the charges have been due and unpaid for at least 30 days.
   (C)   When it becomes necessary for the village to discontinue utility
service to a customer for nonpayment of bills, service will be reinstated only
after all bills for service then due have been paid, along with a turn-on
charge in the sum of $25.
§ 50.23 ACCESS TO PREMISES.
   The Utility Superintendent and his or her assistant shall have free access
during proper hours of the day and after reasonable notice, to all parts of
every building in which water is delivered and consumed, to examine the pipes
and fixtures and to ascertain whether or not there is any unnecessary waste of
water. The term PROPER HOURS as used in this section means during an hour when
the occupants are or may reasonably be expected to be awake, dressed, and in
condition to receive visitors.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021)
§ 50.24 CONTAMINATION OF WATER SUPPLY.
   No person shall place in or near or around the reservoir, catch basin, or
any other part of the water works system of this village any dirt, filth, or
impure substance whatsoever, or any substance or fluid by which water shall be
rendered impure, unpalatable, or dangerous for human or animal consumption.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.25 UNINTERRUPTED SERVICE; LIABILITY OF VILLAGE.
   This village shall in no manner be liable for any damages caused by shutting
off the supply of water of any consumer while the system or any part thereof is
undergoing repairs or extensions or caused by freezing of the main or the
breaking of any pipe or valve, or by a shortage of water due to accident, or to
circumstances over which this village has no control, or to an act of God.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021)
§ 50.26 RESTRICTIONS ON USE.
   The right of the consumer to use water under the contract provided for in
this subchapter is subject to such rules and regulations as the Chief of the
Fire Department in this village may make, and subject to such regulations as
the Utility Superintendent shall make to conserve water for the more urgent
needs of the residents of this village in the event of a water shortage.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.27 WATER TURN ON.
   Water shall not be turned on at the curb stop valve except by the Utility
Superintendent or his or her assistant or by his or her permission, except that
any plumber may turn the water on temporarily for the sole purpose of testing
the pipes.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021)
§ 50.28 SHUT-OFF VALVE IN BUILDINGS.
   There shall be a shut-off valve attached to every supply pipe at a point in
the building so as to enable the consumer to shut off water and drain the
pipes.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.29 EXCAVATIONS.
   In making excavations in streets or highways for the laying of service pipes
or making repairs, the planks or pavement, stones, and earth removed must be
deposited in a manner that will occasion the least inconvenience to the public
and provide for passage of water along gutters. No person shall leave any
excavations made in a sidewalk, street, or alley open at any time without a
barricade, and, during the night, warning lights must be maintained at such
excavation. After the service pipes are laid, in filling the opening, the earth
must be laid in layers of not more than nine inches in depth, and each layer
shall be thoroughly tamped and puddled. The streets, sidewalks, and pavements
must be restored to as good condition as previous to making excavation. All
dirt, stones, and rubbish must be removed immediately after completion of the
work. If an excavation in any street, alley, or highway shall be left open or
unfinished for the space of 24 hours or more, if the work shall be improperly
done, or if the rubbish shall not be removed, the Utility Superintendent shall
have the right to finish or correct the work, and the expense incurred shall be
charged to the consumer and shall be paid by the plumber, drain layer, or other
person authorized by the consumer to do the excavating work or by the consumer
before the water is turned on. No main shall be tapped or connection made when
the ground is frozen, except by special permission of the Utility
Superintendent. No person shall make any excavation in any streets or highways
within six feet of any laid water pipe while the ground is frozen or dig up or
uncover so as to expose to the frost any water pipe of this village except
under direction of the Utility Superintendent.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.30 LEAKAGE.
   Any consumer having knowledge of leaking pipes on his or her own premises or
between the commercial main and said premises shall cause them to be repaired
as soon as reasonably possible.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021)
§ 50.31 FIRE HYDRANTS.
   All hydrants erected by said village for the purpose of extinguishing fires
are hereby declared to be public hydrants, and no person or persons other than
members of the Fire Department in the acting discharge of their duties as such,
or the Utility Superintendent, or some person acting directly through his or
her order, shall open said hydrants or attempt to draw water from the same or
at any time uncover or remove any protection from any of said hydrants or in
any manner interfere with the same, and no person authorized to open hydrants
shall delegate his or her authority to another, or lend out, or suffer any
person to take the wrenches in his or her possession or control, or allow the
same to be taken from any house in said village except for the purpose strictly
connected with the Fire Department, or as they may accompany fire apparatus on
occasion of fire.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.32 WATER STEALING.
   No person shall tamper with any meter for the purpose of causing it to read
inaccurately, nor attempt by any means to divert water from the service pipe so
that it will not pass through the proper meter, nor to procure water from the
water works for any premises while the water service thereto is disconnected
for non-payment of water rates or pursuant to §
50.99.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.33 WATER WASTE.
   No person shall deliberately waste water. The Utility Superintendent may
make and publish such regulation as he or she deems necessary to determine what
constitutes deliberate waste of water, but such regulations when made shall
apply uniformly throughout the village.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.34 NO OBLIGATION OUTSIDE CORPORATE LIMITS.
   The village is not obligated to furnish water service to premises outside
the corporate limits, and shall not, unless it is able to do so without
overloading its pumps and without curtailing any reasonable use of water within
the corporate limits of the village.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021)
§ 50.35 PLUMBING RESTRICTIONS.
   No persons other than the Utility Superintendent or his or her assistant or
a licensed plumber under his or her direction shall set meters, tap commercial
mains, or make a connection to the water service of this village. No person
shall install plumbing or water service in this village unless licensed.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.36 LIEN.
   In addition to all other remedies, if a consumer shall for any reason remain
indebted to the village for water service furnished, such amount due, together
with any rents and charges in arrears, shall be considered delinquent, and a
lien will be placed upon the real estate for which the same was used. The
Village Clerk shall notify in writing, or cause to be notified in writing, all
owners of premises, or their agents, whenever their tenants or lessees are 60
days or more delinquent in the payment of water rent.
(Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-2021)
WATER CONSERVATION MEASURES
§ 50.50 PURPOSE.
   The purpose of this subchapter is to provide for the declaration of a water
supply watch, warning, or emergency and the implementation of voluntary and
mandatory water conservation measures throughout the village in the event such
a watch, warning, or emergency is declared.
(Ord. 340, passed 5-4-2004)
§ 50.51 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   CLASS 1. Water used for outdoor watering, either public or private, for
gardens, lawns, trees, shrubs, plants, golf courses, playing fields, swimming
pools, or other recreational areas; or the washing of motor vehicles, boats,
trailers, or the exterior of any building or structure.
   CLASS 2. Water used for any commercial or industrial, including agricultural
purposes, except water actually necessary to maintain the health and personal
hygiene of bona fide employees which such employees are engaged in the
performance of their duties at their place of employment.
   CLASS 3. Domestic usage other than that which would be included in either
Classes 1 or 2.
   CLASS 4. Water necessary only to sustain human life and the lives of
domestic pets, and maintain standards of hygiene and sanitation.
   CUSTOMER. The customer of record using water for any purpose from the
village’s water distribution system and for which either a regular charge is
made, or in the case of coin sales, a cash charge is made at the site of
delivery.
   WASTE OF WATER. Includes, but is not limited to:
      (1)   Permitting water to escape down a gutter, ditch, or other surface
drain; or
      (2)   Failure to repair a controllable leak of water due to defective
plumbing.
   WATER. Water available to the village for treatment by virtue of its water
rights, or any treated water introduced by the village into its water
distribution system, including water offered for sale at any coin-operated
site.
(Ord. 340, passed 5-4-2004)
§ 50.52 DECLARATION OF WATER WATCH.
   Whenever the Village Board finds that conditions indicate that the
probability of a drought or some other condition causing a major water supply
shortage is rising, it shall be empowered to declare that a water watch exists,
and that it shall take steps to inform the public and ask for voluntary
reductions in water use. Such a watch shall be deemed to continue until it is
declared by the Village Board to have ended.
(Ord. 340, passed 5-4-2004)
§ 50.53 DECLARATION OF WATER WARNING.
   Whenever the Village Board finds that drought conditions or some other
conditions causing a major water supply shortage are present and supplies are
starting to decline, it shall be empowered to declare that a water warning
exists, and that it will recommend restrictions on nonessential uses during the
period of warning. Such a warning shall be deemed to continue until it is
declared by the Village Board to have ended.
(Ord. 340, passed 5-4-2004)
§ 50.54 DECLARATION OF WATER EMERGENCY.
   Whenever the Village Board finds that an emergency exists by reason of a
shortage of water supply needed for essential uses, it shall be empowered to
declare that a water supply emergency exists, and that it will impose mandatory
restrictions on water use during the period of the emergency. Such an emergency
shall be deemed to continue until it is declared by the Village Board to have
ended.
(Ord. 340, passed 5-4-2004)
§ 50.55 VOLUNTARY CONSERVATION MEASURES.
   Upon the declaration of a water watch or water warning as provided in §§
50.52 and
50.53, the Water Operator is authorized to call on all water consumers to
employ voluntary water conservation measures to limit or eliminate nonessential
water uses including, but not limited to, limitation on the following uses:
   (A)   Sprinkling of water on lawns, shrubs, or trees (including golf
courses);
   (B)   Washing of automobiles;
   (C)   Use of water in swimming pools, fountains, and evaporative air
conditioning systems; and
   (D)   Waste of water.
(Ord. 340, passed 5-4-2004)
§ 50.56 MANDATORY CONSERVATION MEASURES.
   Upon the declaration of a water supply emergency as provided in §
50.54, the Water Operator is also authorized to implement certain mandatory
water conservation measures, including, but not limited to, the following:
   (A)   Suspension of new connections to the village’s water distribution
system, except connections of fire hydrants and those made pursuant to
agreements entered into by the village prior to the effective date of an
emergency;
   (B)   Restrictions on the uses of water in one or more classes of water use,
wholly or in part;
   (C)   Restrictions on the sales of water at coin-operated facilities or
sites;
   (D)   The imposition of water rationing based on any reasonable formula
including, but not limited to, the percentage of normal use and per capita or
per consumer restrictions;
   (E)   Complete or partial bans on the waste of water; and
   (F)   Any combination of the foregoing measures.
(Ord. 340, passed 5-4-2004)
§ 50.57 EMERGENCY WATER RATES.
   Upon the declaration of a water supply emergency as provided in §
50.54, the Village Board shall have the power to adopt emergency water rates by
ordinance designed to conserve water supplies. Such emergency rates may provide
for, but not limited to:
   (A)   Higher charges for increasing usage;
   (B)   Uniform charges for water usage; or
   (C)   Extra charges in excess of a specified level of water use.
(Ord. 340, passed 5-4-2004)
§ 50.58 REGULATIONS.
   During the effective period of any water supply emergency as provided for in
§
50.54, the Chairperson of the Board and/or the Water Operator is empowered to
promulgate such regulations as may be necessary to carry out the provisions of
this subchapter.
(Ord. 340, passed 5-4-2004)
§ 50.59 VIOLATIONS; DISCONNECTION.
   (A)   If the Chairperson of the Board and/or the water operator charged with
the implementation and enforcement of this subchapter learn of any violation of
any water use restrictions imposed pursuant to §§
50.56 and
50.58, a written notice of the violation shall be affixed to the property where
the violation occurred, and the customer of record and any other person known
to the village who is responsible for the violation or its correction shall be
provided with either actual or mailed notice. Such notice shall describe the
violation and order that it be corrected, cured, or abated immediately or
within such specified time as the village determines is reasonable under the
circumstances. If the order is not complied with, the village may terminate
water service to the customer subject to the following procedures.
      (1)   The village shall give the customer notice by mail or actual notice
that water service will be discontinued with a specified time due to the
violation, and that the customer will have the opportunity to appeal the
termination by requesting a meeting with the water operator.
      (2)   If such a meeting is requested by the customer charged with the
violation, he or she shall be given a full opportunity to be heard before
termination is ordered.
      (3)   The water operator shall make findings of fact and order whether
service should continue or be terminated.
   (B)   (1)   A fee of $50 shall be paid for the reconnection of any water
service terminated pursuant to division (A) above.
      (2)   In the event of subsequent violations, the reconnection fee shall
be $200 for the second reconnection and $300 for any additional reconnections.
(Ord. 340, passed 5-4-2004) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.60 EMERGENCY TERMINATION.
   Nothing in this subchapter shall limit the ability of any properly
authorized village official from terminating the supply of water to any or all
customers, upon the determination of such village official, that emergency
termination of water service is required to protect the health and safety of
the public.
(Ord. 340, passed 5-4-2004)
§ 50.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Any person who shall violate or refuse to comply with the enforcement
of any of the provisions of §
50.01 shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be fined not less than
$25 for each offense. A new violation shall be deemed to have been committed
every 24 hours of such failure to comply.
   (C)   Violation of §
50.02(F) shall result in a fine of up to $500 and if the condition exists for
longer than a 24-hour period, it shall be a new and separate offense for every
24 hours that it continues.
   (D)   Any person who shall violate or refuse to comply with the enforcement
of any of the provisions of §
50.04 shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor, and shall be fined no more than
$500 for each offense. A new violation shall be deemed to have been committed
every 24 hours of such failure to comply.
   (E)   Any person violating any provision of any section of §§
50.15 through
50.36, including the regulations promulgated by the Utility Superintendent
under §§
50.26 and
50.33, shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor, and, upon conviction thereof,
be fined in any sum not less than $100 nor more than $500, and assessed the
court costs of prosecution, and, if the person convicted is a consumer, the
Utility Superintendent, if so directed by the Chairperson and Board shall
disconnect the water service to him or her until he or she furnishes
satisfactory assurance that he or she will not violate such provision in the
future.
   (F)   Violations of §§
50.50 through
50.60 shall be a municipal offense and may be prosecuted in county court. Any
person so charged and found guilty in county court of violating the provisions
of §§
50.50 through
50.60 shall be guilty of a municipal offense. Each day’s violation shall
constitute a separate offense. The penalty for an initial violation shall be a
mandatory fine of $100. In addition, such customer may be required by the court
to service a definite term of confinement in the county jail which shall be
fixed by the court and which shall not exceed 30 days. The penalty for a second
or subsequent conviction shall be a mandatory fine of $200. In addition, such
customer shall serve a definite term of confinement in the county jail, which
shall be fixed by the court and which shall not exceed 30 days.
(Ord. 295, passed - -; Ord. 340, passed 5-4-2004; Ord. 346, passed 12-6-2005;
Ord. 359, passed 3-2-2010; Ord. 360, passed 3-2-2010; Ord. 2021-1, passed 1-5-
2021)

51.07   Connection with storm sewers; sump required
   
51.08   Fines for permits, inspection, and other services
Sewer Rates
   
51.20   Rates established; lien against property
   
51.21   Terms defined
   
51.22   Rates; amount
   
51.23   When due
 
   
51.99   Penalty
SEWER SYSTEM
§ 51.01 CONFORMITY.
   All connections with the public sewer of the village or the construction or
modification of appurtenances to sewers or sewer connections shall be made in
accordance with the provisions of this subchapter.
(Ord. 224, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.02 INSPECTOR; DUTIES.
   The Water Commissioner shall be ex-officio Sewer Inspector for the village,
who shall have general supervision of the sanitary and storm sewer systems and
the sewage disposal plant. It shall be his or her duty to supervise all
building of laterals and determine the grades therefor, and give permits for
and supervise all sewer connections. He or she shall receive such compensation
as the Board shall from time to time determine.
(Ord. 224, passed 10-5-1971)
§ 51.03 CONNECTION REGULATIONS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person other than the Sewer Inspector or
persons in his or her employ, or persons operating under special contract with
the village, or a duly licensed plumber, to open, uncover, or make any
connection with the sewer systems of said village, or to lay any sewer pipes or
attach or modify any fixtures or appurtenances which are in any manner attached
to, or used in connection with, the public sewer systems of said village, other
than such as are on privately owned property.
(Ord. 224, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.04 EXCAVATIONS AND OTHER WORK.
   No excavations or tenches for sewer pipes, or work in connection with such
pipes, attachments, appurtenances, or modifications thereof, other than on
privately owned property, shall be done without a special permit issued by the
Sewer Inspector.
(Ord. 224, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.05 ENTERING OR OPENING MANHOLES.
   Entering or opening manholes, except by the Sewer Inspector or with his or
her express permission, is strictly prohibited.
(Ord. 224, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.06 PRIVATE SEWER CONNECTIONS.
   The following rules and regulations relating to the sanitary sewer system
are hereby adopted and approved.
   (A)   In making private connections with the public sewer, the plumber, with
the assistance of the Sewer Inspector, shall first locate the “Y” joint in the
main sewer to which the connection is to be made, and uncover the same.
Immediately after such “Y” joint has been located and uncovered, he or she
shall make the connection therewith and then proceed to excate from the main
sewer, by the shortest route, to the premises to be served. The work of
connection with the main sewer shall be under the direct supervision of the
Sewer Inspector. Any joints made with the main sewer shall be left uncovered
until inspected and approved by the Sewer Inspector. Any work disapproved by
the Sewer Inspector shall, upon written notice, be promptly remedied.
   (B)   Trenches in streets and alleys shall be excavated so as to impede
public travel as little as possible. Gutters shall be left in such condition as
to allow the escape of water.
   (C)   Red lights or flares shall be kept around all unfinished work at
night, and sufficient barricades against accident shall be placed around the
excavation at all times.
   (D)   All trenches shall be properly braced, and the person excavating shall
be liable for all damages arising by reason of any neglect in this respect.
   (E)   Work in streets and alleys must not be unnecessarily delayed. Should
an excavation in any street or alley be left open or unfinished for the space
of 24 hours, or should the work be improperly done, or excavated material not
be removed, the Sewer Inspector shall finish or correct the work, and the
expense incurred shall be charged to the consumer and paid by him or her before
he or she shall be allowed to use the sewer facilities.
   (F)   The refilling of all trenches shall be done in uniform layers of not
exceeding nine inches and thoroughly tamped, so as to replace all excavated
material and leave the surface in as good condition as found before the
commencement of the work.
   (G)   In the event of the settling of a refilled excavation within one year
after being refilled, the Sewer Inspector shall have the right and it shall be
his or her duty to require restoration by the party who made such excavation or
by the property owner for whom said work was done.
   (H)   Changes of directions of pipes must be made by properly curved pipe
and not by edging or cutting.
   (I)   The Sewer Inspection shall have access at all times to any premises or
building connected with any sewer, to examine the same.
   (J)   All fixtures connected with the sewer shall be equipped with suitable
traps, and whenever the Sewer Inspector shall deem it necessary, screens shall
also be used to prevent entrance of objectionable matter.
   (K)   No one shall deposit or cause or permit to be deposited in any vessel
or receptacle connected with the public sewers, any matter or thing whatsoever
that will tend to obstruct the sewer pipes or impede free passage of the
legitimate contents thereof.
(Ord. 224, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.07 CONNECTION WITH STORM SEWERS; SUMP REQUIRED.
   No connection shall be made from privately owned or operated property with
the storm sewer system except by special permit granted by the Sewer Inspector,
and when required by him or her, there shall be constructed by the property
owner a sump through which all sewer water shall pass before entering the
sewer, which sump shall be constructed as follows.
   (A)   A pit shall be constructed of concrete not less than five feet long,
two and one-half feet wide, and four feet deep, inside measurements.
   (B)   Extending across the pit from side to side there shall be constructed
a vertical baffle wall constructed and located not less than two feet from the
outlet end of the pit and extending downward from the top of the pit to a point
not less than eight inches below the level of the outlet.
   (C)   No inlet to the sump shall be permitted between the baffle wall and
the outlet end shall have a solid metal cover held in position by bolts
securely set in the walls of the sump. Such sump shall be constructed under the
supervision of the Sewer Inspector and shall be subject to periodical
inspection by him or her.
(Ord. 224, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.08 FINES FOR PERMITS, INSPECTION, AND OTHER SERVICES.
   The Sewer Inspector shall receive a fee of $25 for each permit issued by him
or her under the provisions of this subchapter. Such fee shall be paid by the
plumber applying therefor and at the time of application, and such fee shall be
deemed to cover the services of such Sewer Inspector in issuing the permit and
making the necessary records in connection therewith and the same shall also
cover his or her services in locating the “Y” joint and inspecting and
approving the connection therewith.
(Ord. 224, passed 10-5-1971; Ord. 254, passed 6-9-1980)
SEWER RATES
§ 51.20 RATES ESTABLISHED; LIEN AGAINST PROPERTY.
   There are hereby established just and equitable rates or charges to be paid
to the village for the use of the sewage system of the village by each consumer
whose premises are served thereby. If the charges so established are not paid
when due, such sum may be recovered by the village in an action at law, or it
may be certified to the County Clerk and assessed as a lien against the
premises served, and collected or returned in the same manner as other village
taxes are certified, assessed, collected, and returned.
(Ord. 366, passed 12-7-2010)
§ 51.21 TERMS DEFINED.
   The word CONSUMER is used in this subchapter to include all users of the
village sewage system, and the owners and tenants of real estate and building
connected with the village sewage system and served thereby who in any manner
discharge waste or sanitary sewage in any form either directly or indirectly
into the sanitary sewage system of the village.
(Ord. 366, passed 12-7-2010)
§ 51.22 RATES; AMOUNT.
   Rates shall be established by resolution as established by the Village
Board, and shall be available for public inspection.
(Ord. 366, passed 12-7-2010)
§ 51.23 WHEN DUE.
   Bills for the rental or use charges as made by this subchapter shall be
rendered at the same time as water bills are rendered by the village, and all
charges not paid on or before water charges by the village are required to be
paid shall be deemed to be delinquent, and the sewer service shall be
discontinued in the same manner that water service is shut off for delinquent
water bills.
(Ord. 366, passed 12-7-2010)
§ 51.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Any person violating any of the provisions of §§
51.01 through
51.08 or any of the regulations in connection therewith, or who shall fail or
neglect to comply with any such provisions, rules, or regulations, upon
conviction shall be fined not less than $100 nor more than $500 for each
offense and $25 for each day such person shall continue in violation thereof,
and shall pay the costs of prosecution.
(Ord. 224, passed 10-5-1971; Ord. 254, passed 6-9-1980)

GENERAL TRAFFIC PROVISIONS
§ 70.01 DEFINITIONS.
   The words and phrases used in this traffic code pertaining to motor vehicles
and traffic regulations, shall be construed as defined in state statutes, as
now existing or as hereafter amended, unless the context otherwise requires;
and, if not so defined, the common meaning of such words and phrases shall
prevail.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.02 TRACTORS.
   No tractor shall be operated on or over any paved street or over any
concrete sidewalk in said village unless it is equipped with rubber tires or
with smooth drive wheels or smooth tracks, without protecting such street or
walk from injury.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.03 PARADES.
   No motor vehicle shall be driven through a parade which has been authorized
by the Chairperson. No parade shall take place within the corporate limits of
this village unless authorized by the Chairperson, but in determining whether
to authorize or not authorize a parade, the Chairperson shall not discriminate
between political, religious, or racial groups, except that he or she shall not
authorize a parade by any organization which advocates the overthrow by violent
means of the government of the United States or of the government of the state
or by any group affiliated with such an organization.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.04 FUNERAL PROCESSIONS.
   No vehicles, except police or Fire Department vehicles or ambulances when
responding to emergency calls, shall be driven through a funeral procession or
cortege.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.05 DRIVING IN ALLEYS; BACKING.
   Every motor vehicle which is driven through any alley in said village shall
be brought to a full stop immediately before crossing a street line, whether a
stop sign is exhibited or not, and such vehicle shall not proceed into or cross
the intersecting street until the way is clear of pedestrians and approaching
vehicles, and no motor vehicle shall be backed out of any alley into a street.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES
§ 70.20 LOCATION OF STOP SIGNS.
   The Village Board may, from time to time by resolution, designate the
location of stop signs at any intersection or portion of an intersection of any
street.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021)
§ 70.21 REGULATIONS OF TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES.
   The Village Board may, by resolution, designate, establish, and regulate
business, residential, schools, or other street traffic zones; speed limits;
restricted, prohibited, or limited parking zones; manner of parking vehicles;
arterial highways; pedestrian crossings; traffic lanes and direction of travel
on streets and alleys including one-way traffic streets and alleys, and shall
provide for the erection, construction, and maintenance of appropriate signs,
signals, markers, or lights giving proper notice thereof.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021)
§ 70.22 STOP SIGNS.
   At every intersection where a stop sign is displayed, vehicles traveling the
street or alley upon which the same is located shall come to a full stop at the
street line of the intersection street, and shall not enter or cross the
intersection street until the way is clear of pedestrians and approaching
vehicles.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.23 SLOW SIGNS.
   The appearance of slow signs at an intersection or elsewhere on the streets
or alleys requires the driver of a motor vehicle to reduce his or her speed to
not more than 15 mph, and maintain such reduced speed until the intersection or
other obstruction is passed.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.24 PROJECTING LOADS TO REAR.
   When any portion of the load of any vehicle extends more than four feet
beyond the rear of such vehicle, a red flag shall be carried by day and a red
light during the period from sunset to sunrise, securely fastened in a
conspicuous manner at the extreme rear end of such load.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.25 YIELD SIGNS.
   At every intersection where a yield sign is displayed, vehicles traveling
the street or alley upon which the same is located shall, on reaching said
intersection, ascertain that there is no vehicular traffic approaching from
either street coming into said intersection, and shall not enter or cross the
intersection street until the way is clear of pedestrians and approaching
traffic.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.26 DEFACING TRAFFIC SIGNS.
   No persons shall within the corporate limits of this village, willfully
deface, injure, remove, or obstruct any official traffic sign, signal, or
marker, whether erected or installed pursuant to an ordinance of this village,
a resolution of the Chairperson and Village Board, a state statute, or a
regulation of the State Department of Roads. The term MARKER as used herein
shall include marks painted on the curb or pavement to designate parking stalls
or loading zones.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
EMERGENCY VEHICLES
§ 70.40 AMBULANCES, POLICE CARS, AND FIRE TRUCKS.
   The drivers of all ambulances, police cars, and fire trucks shall, at all
times in the operation of such cars and trucks, exercise care and diligence to
prevent accident and injury, but shall not be subject to the provision of this
traffic code as to speed and right-of-way, when responding to emergency or
official calls. All ambulances, police cars, and fire trucks, when responding
to emergency or official calls, shall have the right-of-way over all other
vehicles. It shall be the duty of the drivers of all other vehicles of said
village, upon the approach of an ambulance, police car, or fire truck to drive
their cars as close as possible to the right-hand curb and stop, and remain
there until such ambulance, police car, or fire truck has passed. No vehicle in
said village, except by specific direction by the Chief of the Fire Department
or his or her assistant, shall follow or park closer than 500 feet to a fire or
to a fire apparatus responding to a fire call.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.41 OFFICIAL EMERGENCY VEHICLES; EXEMPT.
   The provisions of this traffic code regulating the movement, parking, and
standing of vehicles shall not apply to:
   (A)   Vehicles when operated with due regard for the safety of others under
the direction of the State Patrol, any conservation officer, sheriff, member of
any police department, or any other law enforcement officer, in the chase or
apprehension of violators of the law or of persons charged with or suspected of
any such violation;
   (B)   Fire Department or fire patrol vehicles when traveling in response to
a fire alarm; or
   (C)   Public or private ambulances or vehicles operated by duly licensed
doctors of medicine when traveling to emergencies. This exemption shall not,
however, protect the driver of any such vehicle from the consequences of a
reckless disregard of the safety of others.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021)
§ 70.42 RIGHT-OF-WAY FOR OFFICIAL EMERGENCY VEHICLES.
   Upon the approach of any authorized emergency vehicle, every vehicle shall
immediately stop, except at the time they are on or crossing an intersecting
street, in which event, such vehicle shall run clear of the street intersection
and then stop. Every vehicle along the route of such emergency vehicle shall
immediately move to a position as near the right-hand curb as possible, and
remain therein until such authorized emergency vehicle or vehicles have passed;
provided, said vehicles are operated on official business and the drivers
thereof sound audible signal by bell, siren, or exhaust whistle.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT
§ 70.55 SPEED, GENERALLY.
   No person shall operate a motor vehicle on any street, alley, or other place
within this village at a rate of speed greater than is reasonable and proper,
having regard for the traffic and roadway and the condition of the streets, nor
at such speed as to endanger the life, limb, or property of any person, or in
any event, at a rate of speed greater than 25 mph in the residential district
of this village, and 20 mph in the business district of this village, except
where otherwise indicated by appropriate signs.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.56 SPEED NEAR SCHOOLS.
   It shall be unlawful for the driver of any vehicle, when passing premises in
this village on which school buildings are located and which are used for
school purposes, during school recess or while children are going to or leaving
school during the opening or closing hours, to drive such vehicle at a rate of
speed in excess of 15 mph past such premises, and such driver shall stop at all
stop signs and shall obey all other traffic signs located at or near such
school premises.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.57 TRAFFIC OFFICERS.
   The Chairperson or local law enforcement may, at any time, detail officers
at street intersections to be known as traffic officers. All traffic officers
shall be vested with authority to regulate and control traffic at intersections
to which they are detailed. It shall be their duty to direct the movement of
traffic at such intersections in such manner as will facilitate traffic and
prevent congestion and accidents. It shall be unlawful for any person to
violate any order or signal of any such traffic officer, notwithstanding any
stop signs or other devices which may have been placed at such intersections.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.58 REFUSAL TO OBEY OFFICER.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to refuse or fail to comply with any
lawful order, signal, or direction of a police officer.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.59 POLICE REGULATIONS.
   Traffic on the streets and alleys of the village shall at all times be
subject to the directions of the duly constituted police officers of the
village, and all orders given verbally by any police officer or traffic officer
of the said village shall be observed and obeyed, with any traffic or parking
regulations prescribed by the Chairperson and Board of said village, and
communicated by means of conspicuous signs placed upon the streets, shall be
observed and obeyed by owners and operators of motor vehicles. In case of a
conflict between the provisions of this traffic code and any orders and
regulations communicated by signs placed conspicuously on the streets, the
latter shall prevail and supersede the provisions of this traffic code.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021)
§ 70.60 CIVIL LIABILITY.
   Nothing in this traffic code shall be construed or pleaded as justifying,
absolving, or rendering blameless, whether directly or indirectly, any person
or persons in charge of or owning any vehicle for any injury or damage to
persons or property due to recklessness, incompetency, or negligence in the
operation of said vehicle.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021)
§ 70.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this traffic code for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Any person violating any provision of this traffic code, the penalty
for which is not otherwise expressly provided, shall on conviction thereof, be
fined in any sum not exceeding $200 and assessed the court costs of
prosecution.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021)

PROHIBITIONS
§ 71.01 OPERATION BY CERTAIN PERSONS PROHIBITED.
   No motor vehicle shall be operated or be permitted to be operated by any
person not having a valid operator’s license, or by any person under the
influence of intoxicating liquor or any drug in violation of Neb. RS 60-6,196.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 71.02 RECKLESS DRIVING.
   No vehicle shall be driven, used, operated, parked, or stopped within this
village in such a manner as to indicate either a willful or wanton disregard
for the safety of persons or property, and every person so doing shall be
deemed guilty of reckless driving and on conviction thereof shall be fined not
less than $50 nor more than $200 and assessed the court costs of prosecution.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 71.03 DUMPING IN STREETS.
   No person shall throw, deposit, dump, or leave or cause to be thrown,
deposited, dumped, or left upon any street, alley, or sidewalk in this village
any rubbish, trash, debris, refuse, sewage, dead animal, glass, crockery,
tacks, nails, or any sharp or broken substance whatsoever.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
Cross-reference:
   Improper disposal of waste, see §
91.01
§ 71.04 DRIVING OVER SIDEWALK SPACE.
   The driver of any vehicle shall not drive over the curb line, and shall not
drive within any sidewalk space, except at a permanent or temporary driveway.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 71.05 DRIVING OVER NEWLY LAID PAVEMENT PROTECTED BY BARRIER.
   (A)   No person shall ride or drive any vehicle over or across any pavement
or asphalt newly laid or repaired which has not been in place for a period of
12 hours and where there has been a barrier placed around or across it.
   (B)   No pedestrian shall walk, run, or otherwise go over or across such
pavement as set forth above.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 71.06 REPAIR OF MOTOR VEHICLES IN STREET.
   No person shall repair any motor vehicle while the same is standing on any
street or alley, in said village, except in case of emergency.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
OPERATION OF VEHICLES
§ 71.20 BRAKES, HORN, LIGHTS.
   (A)   Brakes.
      (1)   Every motor vehicle when operated upon any alley or street of this
village shall be equipped with brakes adequate to control the movements of and
to stop and to hold such vehicle, including two separate means of applying the
brakes, each of which means shall be effective to apply the brakes to at least
two wheels and so constructed that no part which is liable to failure shall be
common to the two, except that a motorcycle need to be equipped with only one
brake. All such brakes shall be maintained at all times in good working order.
      (2)   It shall be unlawful for any owners or operators of any motor
vehicle to operate such motor vehicle upon an alley or street of this village
unless the brake equipment thereon qualifies in the following respects with
regard to maximum stopping distances from a speed of 20 mph on dry asphalt or
concrete pavement free from loose materials as hereinafter set forth:
         (a)   Two wheel brakes, maximum stopping distance: 40 feet;
         (b)   Four or more wheel brakes, vehicles up to 7,000 pounds gross
weight, maximum stopping distance: 30 feet;
         (c)   Four or more wheel brakes, vehicles over 7,000 pounds gross
weight, maximum stopping distance: 35 feet;
         (d)   All hand parking or emergency brakes, vehicles up to 7,000
pounds gross weight, maximum stopping distance: 55 feet; and
         (e)   All hand parking or emergency brakes, vehicles over 7,000 pounds
gross weight, maximum stopping distance: 65 feet.
      (3)   All braking distances specified in division (A)(2) above shall
apply to all vehicles, whether unloaded or loaded, to the maximum capacity
permitted by law.
      (4)   The retarding force of one side of the vehicle shall not exceed the
retarding force on the opposite side so as to prevent the vehicle stopping in a
straight line.
   (B)   Horn.
      (1)   Every motor vehicle when operated upon an alley or street of this
village shall be equipped with a horn in good working order capable of emitting
sound audible under normal conditions from a distance of not less than 200
feet; and it shall be unlawful, except as otherwise provided in this division
(B), for any vehicle to be equipped with or for any person to use upon a
vehicle any siren, exhaust, compression, or spark plug whistle, or for any
person at any time to use a horn other than as a reasonable warning, or to make
any unnecessary or unreasonable loud or harsh sound by means of a horn or other
warning device.
      (2)   All Police and Fire Department vehicles and every ambulance used
for emergency calls shall be equipped with a bell, siren, or exhaust whistle of
a type approved by the State Department of Motor Vehicles.
   (C)   Lights.
      (1)   Every motor vehicle upon an alley or street within this village
during the period from sunset to sunrise, and at any other time when there is
not sufficient light to render clearly discernible persons or vehicles upon the
alleys or streets of this village at a distance of 500 feet ahead, shall be
equipped with lighted front and rear lamps as respectively required in this
division (C) for different classes of vehicles.
      (2)   Every motor vehicle, other than a motorcycle, road roller, road
machinery or farm tractor, shall be equipped with two or more head lamps, at
the front of and on opposite sides of the motor vehicle and with a lamp on the
rear exhibiting a red light visible, under normal atmospheric conditions, from
a distance of at least 500 feet to the rear of such vehicle which head lamps
shall comply with the requirements and limitations set forth in Neb. RS 60-
6,221 and 60-6,223 and, except as to acetylene head lamps, shall be of a type
which has been approved by the State Department of Motor Vehicles.
      (3)   Every motorcycle shall be equipped with at least one and not more
than two head lamps and with a lamp on the rear exhibiting a red light visible,
under normal atmospheric conditions, from a distance of at least 500 feet to
the rear of such motor vehicle, which head lamp or lamps shall comply with the
requirements and limitations set forth in Neb. RS 60-6,221 and 60-6,223 and
except as to acetylene head lamps, shall be of a type which has been approved
by the State Department of Motor Vehicles.
      (4)   It shall be unlawful for any owner or operator of any motor vehicle
to operate such vehicle upon an alley or street of this village unless:
         (a)   The condition of the lamps and electric circuit shall be such as
to give substantially normal light output;
         (b)   The tail light shall show red directly to the rear, glass
therein shall be unbroken, the lamp shall be securely fastened, and its
electric circuit free from grounds and shorts;
         (c)   If equipped with spot lamps, the number shall be limited to not
more than one spot lamp;
         (d)   If equipped with auxiliary driving lamps, the number shall be
limited to not more than two auxiliary driving lamps, and such auxiliary lamps,
if used, must be mounted on the front at a point not less than 15 inches above
the level surface upon which the vehicle stands, and every such auxiliary lamp
or lamps shall meet the statutory requirements for head lamps;
         (e)   If equipped with any lighting device, other than head lamps,
spot lamp, or auxiliary driving lamps, which projects a beam of light of an
intensity greater than 25 candle power, such lighting device shall be so
directed that no part of the beam therefrom will strike the level of the
surface on which the vehicle stands at a distance of more than 50 feet from the
vehicle; and
         (f)   If equipped with side cowl or fender lamps, the number shall be
limited to two such lamps, and each such side cowl or fender lamp shall emit an
amber or white light.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 71.21 BUMPERS.
   No person shall operate a motor vehicle upon the streets or alleys of this
village which is not equipped with conventional bumpers on the front and rear.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 71.22 DIMMING LIGHTS.
   Whenever any person operating a motor vehicle equipped with head lamps
constructed and adjusted to project glaring or dazzling light to persons in
front of such head lamps, on any street or alley of this village shall meet
another person operating a motor vehicle in the opposite direction, they shall,
on signal of said other person, forthwith dim the head lamps of his or her
motor vehicle or tilt the beams of glaring or dazzling light projecting
therefrom downward so as not to confuse the vision of said other operator.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 71.23 FRONT SEAT LOAD.
   (A)   No motor vehicle shall have more than three adult passengers in the
driver’s compartment thereof, and in no event more than four persons occupying
the driver’s compartment.
   (B)   In construing this section, an ADULT PERSONS shall be deemed to be any
persons 12 years old or more.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
TURNING, PASSING, AND STOPPING
§ 71.35 RIGHT SIDE OF STREET.
   Motor vehicles shall at all times be driven on the right side of the center
of the street, except when it is necessary to cross the center line in
overtaking and passing another vehicle.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 71.36 VEHICLES TO KEEP RIGHT WHEN MEETING.
   Vehicles meeting shall pass each other to the right.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 71.37 VEHICLES TO KEEP LEFT WHEN PASSING.
   The driver of a vehicle overtaking another vehicle traveling in the same
direction shall pass to the left of such vehicle, but no vehicle shall pass
another on an intersection of streets.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 71.38 LEFT TURNS.
   When a left turn is intended to be made, it shall be the duty of the driver
to, at least 50 feet before beginning said turn, signal his or her intention by
extending his or her hand and arm horizontally from the left side of the
vehicle or by a signal lamp or device of a type approved by the State
Department of Roads.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 71.39 RIGHT-OF-WAY.
   Motor vehicles traveling on streets which are protected by stop signs shall
have the right-of-way over all other vehicles entering or crossing other
streets, but motor vehicles driving on streets which are not protected by stop
signs shall yield the right-of-way to vehicles approaching on intersecting
streets from the right, and shall have the right-of-way over those approaching
from the left when such approaching vehicle shall reach the intersection at
approximately the same time. In all other cases on streets which are not
protected by stop signs, the vehicle reaching the intersection first shall have
the right-of-way. The driver of a vehicle approaching but not having entered an
intersection shall yield the right-of-way to a vehicle within such intersection
whose driver has signaled his or her intent to turn to the left across the line
of travel of such first mentioned vehicle. The driver of any vehicle upon any
street shall yield the right-of-way of a pedestrian crossing said street within
a clearly marked crosswalk of any regular pedestrian crossing, including the
prolongation of a lateral boundary line of the adjacent sidewalk at the end of
a block, except at intersections where the movement of traffic is being
controlled by traffic officers or traffic direction devices. Every pedestrian
crossing a street within any point other than a pedestrian crossing, crosswalk,
or intersection shall yield the right-of-way to all vehicles upon the street.
The driver of any vehicle traveling at an unlawful rate of speed shall forfeit
any right-of-way which he or she may otherwise have hereunder.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 71.40 ENGINE BRAKING.
   (A)   Definition. For the purposes of this section, ENGINE BRAKE shall be
defined as a device that converts a power producing engine into a power-
absorbing air compressor, resulting in a net energy loss.
(Neb. RS 60-680(1)(v))
   (B)   Engine breaking prohibited. It shall be unlawful for any person to use
engine brakes within the village limits of the village.
(Neb. RS 60-680(1)(v))
   (C)   Violation. Any person violating this section shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof, be fined up to $100 and assessed the
court costs of prosecution.
(Ord. 2017-4, passed 5-2-2017)
CHAPTER 72: PARKING REGULATIONS
Section
   
72.01   Parking, generally
   
72.02   Allowing clearance for traffic
   
72.03   Direction of traffic

§ 72.01 PARKING, GENERALLY.
   No motor vehicle shall be parked or left standing for a period longer than
three minutes on the street unless parked either where parallel parking has
been marked on the curb, with the right side of the vehicle not more than 12
inches from the curb line or where diagonal parking has been marked on the curb
and street, with the vehicle parked between the diagonal lines with the right
front tire touching the curb. Where parking lines have been placed in the
center of the street, cars shall be parked in the spaces between such lines. In
the paved sections of the village, non-parking spaces may be designated by red
or yellow paint on the curb or by appropriate signs adopted by the Village
Board.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-6-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 72.02 ALLOWING CLEARANCE FOR TRAFFIC.
   No motor vehicles shall be parked on any street in such a position that
there is not a clearance of at least ten feet between such vehicle and the curb
or another vehicle on the opposite side of the street.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-6-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 72.03 DIRECTION OF TRAFFIC.
   No person shall park and leave standing any vehicle or approach the curb
with a vehicle, except when it is headed in the direction of the traffic on
that side of the street.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-6-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 72.04 ALLEYS.
   No vehicle shall be parked in any alley so as to obstruct free passage of
other vehicles in said alley, and in no event shall any vehicle be parked on an
alley for any purpose other than to load or unload, and then only during the
time necessary for such loading and unloading, which shall not exceed 30
minutes.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-6-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 72.05 NEAR FIRE HYDRANT; OTHER OBSTRUCTIONS.
   No car or other vehicle shall be parked within 20 feet of any fire hydrant,
except in a designated parking place, or in front of the driveway of any
buildings in which fire apparatus of said village shall be stored or in front
of driveways provided for filling stations, garages, or other places of
business, or residences, or parked in such a manner that any portion thereof
shall be in front of any alley entrance or in any street intersection or across
any sidewalk or crosswalk.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-6-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 72.06 NEAR INTERSECTION.
   No vehicle shall be placed or left standing for any purpose whatsoever
within a distance of 25 feet from any street intersection, which distance shall
be measured from the point of intersection of curb lines, and if there are no
curbs, from within 15 feet of the intersection. This section shall not apply
where parking spaces are designated within the designated area.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-6-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 72.07 STORING VEHICLES IN STREET.
   No truck, truck-tractor, or farm truck shall be parked upon any street,
alley, or public place for more than 24 hours.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-6-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 72.08 UNLAWFULLY PARKED AND ABANDONED CARS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person, partnership, firm, or corporation
to park any vehicle or means of conveyance upon the streets, alleys, or rights-
of-way, in the village which does not display a current and up-to-date vehicle
license issued by the State Department of Roads.
   (B)   If any vehicles or means of conveyance shall be found unattended in
any street, alley, right-of-way, or portion thereof which vehicle or means of
conveyance is improperly or unlawfully parked according to the restrictions
herein, the police officers and street employees are hereby empowered to remove
the same, and they are further empowered to remove any vehicle found as
aforesaid if the operator fails to remove the same upon being notified to do
so. Whenever a vehicle or conveyance has been placed or parked upon the
streets, alleys, or rights-of-way, or portion thereof, in violation of the
provisions of this chapter, or whenever the owner or operator fails to promptly
remove his or her vehicle or conveyance which is in violation upon notification
to do so, the expense of such removal may be charged to such owner or operator.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-6-2021) Penalty, see §
70.99

BICYCLES
§ 73.01 HOLDING ONTO MOVING VEHICLES AND CARRYING PASSENGERS.
   No persons riding a bicycle shall take hold of or hold onto any other moving
vehicle. No persons operating a motor vehicle or bicycle shall carry another
person on said vehicle in front of the operator, except in the event of an
emergency involving the personal health or safety of the persons thus carried
or some other person.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-6-2021) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.02 PEDESTRIAN RIGHT-OF-WAY.
   Pedestrians on the sidewalks or crossing streets or alleys at the crossing
shall have the right-of-way over persons riding bicycles, and riders of the
bicycles shall accord said right-of-way to them.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-6-2021) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.03 REFLECTORS REQUIRED.
   No persons shall ride a bicycle in this village during the period after
sunset and before sunrise unless said bicycle is equipped with either lights or
reflectors, both front and rear, in good working order and clearly visible for
a distance of at least 300 feet.
(Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-6-2021) Penalty, see §
73.99
ALL-TERRAIN AND UTILITY-TYPE VEHICLES
§ 73.15 DEFINITIONS.
   An ALL-TERRAIN VEHICLE or a UTILITY-TYPE VEHICLE as the terms are defined in
the State Rules of the Road Neb. RS 60-6,355 may be operated on the village
streets and alleys but not on the sidewalks of the village; provided, the
operation complies with the conditions set out in §
73.16.
(Ord. 367, passed 1-4-2011)
§ 73.16 CONDITIONS FOR OPERATION.
   The conditions for the operation of an all-terrain vehicle or a utility-type
vehicle within the village are as follows.
   (A)   The operation must occur only between the hours of sunrise and sunset.
   (B)   Any person operating an all-terrain vehicle or a utility-type vehicle
shall have a valid Class O operator’s license or a farm permit as provided in
the State Rules of the Road Neb. RS 60-4,126.
   (C)   The operator shall have liability insurance coverage for the all-
terrain vehicle or the utility-type vehicle while operating the all-terrain
vehicle or utility-type vehicle on a public road, and the operator shall
provide proof of such insurance to any peace officer requesting such proof
within five days of such a request.
   (D)   The operator shall not operate the all-terrain vehicle or the utility-
type vehicle at a speed in excess of 30 mph and if the speed limit posted in
the village is less than 30 mph for a motor vehicle, the operator shall not
operate the all-terrain vehicle or utility-type vehicle at a speed in excess of
the speed limit provided by the village ordinances for motor vehicles.
   (E)   The all-terrain vehicle or utility-type vehicle shall have a headlight
and a taillight and these must be on. The all-terrain vehicle or utility-type
vehicle shall be equipped with a bicycle safety flag that extends not less than
five feet above ground, attached to the rear of the vehicle. The safety flag
shall be triangular in shape with an area of not less than 30 square inches and
shall be day-glow in color.
(Ord. 367, passed 1-4-2011) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.17 PARADES.
   An all-terrain vehicle or utility-type vehicle may be operated without
complying with the requirements of §
73.16 in parades that have been authorized by the state or by a political
subdivision of the state.
(Ord. 367, passed 1-4-2011) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of §§
73.01 through
73.03, the penalty for which is not otherwise expressly provided, shall on
conviction thereof, be fined in any sum not exceeding $200 and assessed the
court costs of prosecution.
   (B)   Any person violating any provisions of §§
73.15 through
73.17 shall be fined in a sum not to exceed $500 and be assessed the court
costs of prosecution, except that if such person is convicted of a second or
subsequent offense within any period of one year, that person shall be fined a
minimum of $200.
(Ord. 367, passed 1-4-2011; Ord. 2021-3, passed 7-14-2021)
