GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 111.01 DEFINITIONS.
   Unless the context otherwise requires, the words and phrases defined in Neb.
RS 53-103.01 to 53-103.43, or as hereafter amended or revised, shall be adopted
for the purposes of construing this chapter; and said words and phrases are
hereby incorporated by reference the same as though copied at full length
herein.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023)
§ 111.02 RESTRICTIONS ON PLACE OF CONSUMPTION.
   No person(s) shall drink or consume alcoholic liquors on any street or alley
within the village or inside any vehicle on any street or alley within the
village or in any place open to the general public other than a premises having
a Class A or a Class C license as those terms are defined in Neb. RS 53-124. No
person shall consume alcoholic liquor on a premises having such license except
during the periods of time when the liquor consumed may be lawfully sold on
said premises and for 15 minutes after the expiration of such periods.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.03 OCCUPATION TAX.
   (A)   For the purpose of raising revenue, there is hereby levied an annual
occupation tax upon the following occupations carried on within this village,
and a state license fee, to wit:
      (1)   Class B license, beer license only for consumption off premises,
regardless of alcoholic content, sales in the original packages only:
         (a)   License fee: $100; and
         (b)   Occupation tax: $50.
      (2)   Class C license, alcoholic liquors within the corporate limits of
the village for consumption on the premises and off the premises, sales in
original packages only:
         (a)   License fee: $300; and
         (b)   Occupation tax: $120.
      (3)   Class D license, alcoholic liquors including beer, regardless of
alcoholic content, within the corporate limits of the village for consumption
off the premises, sales in original packages only:
         (a)   License fee: $200; and
         (b)   Occupation tax: $120.
      (4)   Class I license, alcoholic liquor, inside the corporate limits of
the village, for consumption on the premises:
         (a)   License fee: $250; and
         (b)   Occupation tax: $120.
   (B)   The occupation tax year shall coincide with the license year and no
new or renewal license shall be delivered by the Village Clerk until the
occupation tax is paid. There shall be no pro rata reduction in the tax in the
event the taxpayer engages in one or more of the occupations above set out for
less than a full occupation tax year.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023)
LICENSE REQUIREMENTS
§ 111.15 LICENSE REQUIRED.
   No person shall manufacture for sale, sell, keep for sale, barter, or
exchange under any pretext any alcoholic liquor within this village unless said
person shall have a valid license therefor as provided by the State Liquor
Control Act as amended.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.16 APPROVAL OR DENIAL OF LICENSE.
   (A)   The Village Clerk, or his or her designee, be and is hereby designated
as the agent of the village to determine whether a special designated liquor
license is to be approved or denied in accordance with the criteria established
in division (B) below.
   (B)   The following guidelines will be applied by the Village Clerk in
reviewing applications for special designated liquor licenses for the
consumption of alcoholic liquors.
      (1)   An application for a special designated liquor license will be
presented to the Village Board when:
         (a)   The applicant for a special designated liquor license has not
previously applied for a special designated license; or
         (b)   The special designated liquor license is requested for activity
on property owned or operated by the village.
      (2)   An application for a special designated liquor license will be
approved by the Village Clerk only when:
         (a)   Review any recommendation by the Village Police Chief or his or
her designee of the State Liquor Control Commission special designated license
application to ensure adequate levels of security for general safety and the
enforcement of liquor laws;
         (b)   Adequate restroom facilities are available or will be provided;
         (c)   The licensed area will be separated from other areas by a fence,
wall, or similar barrier sufficient to prevent uncontrolled entrance or exit
from the licensed area, if the license is requested for an outdoor area;
         (d)   The granting of such a permit will not create traffic congestion
or hazards and will not violate any of the provisions of this code;
         (e)   The application for special designated liquor license is
submitted for review at least 21 days prior to the event date. The Village
Clerk may deny any application received with insufficient time to complete the
review necessary to make a determination as to whether to approve or deny said
license; and
         (f)   The application otherwise complies with the requirements and
limitations of the State Liquor Control Act.
      (3)   An application for a special designated liquor license will be
denied by the Village Clerk when:
         (a)   The application is made by a corporation, association,
organization, or other entity, whose membership consists of a majority of
individuals who are under the legal drinking age;
         (b)   The area included within a special designated permit is outside
of any fully enclosed structure and/or requires a street closing, except when
the application is made in conjunction with a festival or other similar
sponsored or supported community event; and
         (c)   The application does not satisfy the criteria set forth above
for approval by the Village Clerk.
      (4)   Upon denial of a special designated liquor license, the Village
Clerk, or their designee, shall give the applicant a written statement of the
reason(s) for denial. Any applicant denied a special designated liquor license
based upon the above guidelines, may file with the Village Clerk a written
request for said application to be heard by the Village Board for
consideration. Such request shall be submitted within three business days
following the denial of the license. The request shall be considered at the
next regularly scheduled Village Board meeting.
      (5)   The notice of approval or denial of the license shall be forwarded
to the State Liquor Control Commission in the same manner as if the approval or
denial was issued by the Village Board.
      (6)   At least quarterly, the Village Clerk, or his or her designee,
shall provide the Village Board with a report of all special designated liquor
licenses approved or denied during the preceding months.
      (7)   The guidelines in this division (B) shall be applied to all
applications for special designated liquor licenses for the consumption of
alcoholic liquors. Nothing herein shall preclude the Village Board from
deviating from the above-stated guidelines when exceptional or peculiar
circumstances exist warranting such a deviation. The Village Board may, at any
time, adopt specific criteria to be considered during review of any special
designated liquor license application. Upon adoption, said criteria shall be
considered prior to approval or denial of all applications for special
designated liquor license, whether said approval or denial is administered by
the Village Board or the Village Clerk or his or her designee.
      (8)   The guidelines in this division (B) shall be applied to all
applications for special designated liquor licenses for the consumption of
alcoholic liquors. Any applicant denied a special designated liquor license
based upon the above guidelines may request that such application be heard by
the Village Board of Trustees.
(Ord. 2022-1, passed 1-4-2022)
§ 111.17 REVOCATION OF LICENSE.
   The Village Board of Trustees shall have the power, function, and duty to
cancel or revoke, on its own motion, any license if, upon the same notice and
hearing as provided in §
111.18 and Neb. RS 53-134.04, it determines that the licensee has violated any
of the provisions of the act or any valid and subsisting ordinance, resolution,
rule, or regulation duly enacted, adopted, and promulgated relating to
alcoholic liquor. Such order of cancellation or revocation may be appealed to
the Commission within 30 days after the date of the order by filing a notice of
appeal with the Commission. The Commission shall handle the appeal in a manner
provided for hearing on an application in Neb. RS 53-133.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023)
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see Neb. RS 53-134(6)
§ 111.18 FORM FOR CITIZEN COMPLAINT.
   (A)   The Village Board of Trustees shall have the power, function, and duty
to receive a signed complaint from any citizen within its jurisdiction that any
provision of the act, any rule or regulation adopted and promulgated pursuant
to the act, or any ordinance, resolution, rule, or regulation adopted by the
Village Board has been or is being violated, and to act upon such complaints in
the manner provided in the Act.
   (B)   The following form is hereby prescribed for the use of residents of
the village desiring to complain to the Board of Trustees that any licensee is
violating any provision of the State Liquor Control Act, any regulation
prescribed by the State Liquor Control Commission, or any provision of this
chapter:
To the Chairperson and Board of the Village of Petersburg:
The undersigned respectfully state:
That they believe that ______________________ the holder of a Class _____
license in the Village of Petersburg has violated section(s) of:
__ The Nebraska Liquor Control Act
__ The regulations of the Nebraska Liquor Control Commission
__ The Municipal Code of the Village of Petersburg
(Check one or more)
That the aforesaid belief is based on the following facts, to-wit:
___________________________________________________________________________________
___________________________________________________________________________________
_______________________________________________
STATE OF NEBRASKA      )
                     ) SS.
COUNTY OF BOONE      )
Subscribed in my presence and sworn to before me by, ___________, _________,
_________, _________, and _______________ this ________ day of ______, 20___.
   ___________________________
      Notary Public - Village Clerk
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023)
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see Neb. RS 53-134(3)
§ 111.19 FORMS, CONTINUED; PROCEDURE.
   (A)   The Village Clerk shall cause to be printed an adequate supply of the
forms prescribed in §
111.18, and shall on the request supply one to any resident of the village
desiring to initiate a complaint thereon. Any complaint duly executed on the
aforesaid form by five residents of the village and filed with the Village
Clerk shall be presented by the Clerk to the Board of Trustees at their next
meeting.
   (B)   If the Board is satisfied that the complaint substantially charges a
violation and that from the facts alleged there is reasonable cause for such
belief, they shall, by resolution, set the matter for hearing within ten days
from the date of the meeting at which such determination is made.
   (C)   Said resolution shall state the time and place of said hearing, and
shall direct the County Sheriff to serve the same on the licensee by delivering
to him or her personally a true and certified copy thereof at least 72 hours
prior to the time of hearing.
   (D)   Said resolution shall also state the section or sections of the State
Liquor Control Act, or the regulations of the State Liquor Control Commission,
or of this code alleged to have been violated and the facts on which said
allegation is based, as stated in the complaint.
   (E)   At said hearing, the Village Attorney shall be present, the licensee
shall be present, and may be represented by counsel employed by him or her, the
complainants shall be present and may be represented by counsel employed by
them.
   (F)   The Board shall, within 30 days from the date the complaint is filed,
by resolution, dispose of the complaint which resolution shall be deemed the
final order for purposes of appeal to the State Liquor Control Commission.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023)
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see Neb. RS 53-134.04
§ 111.20 COMPLAINT INITIATED BY BOARD.
   (A)   The Board of Trustees may, on their own motion, by resolution, fix the
time and place for a hearing on whether or not a licensee has violated any
section of the State Liquor Control Act, or any regulations of the State Liquor
Control Commission or of this code, which resolution shall state the section or
sections in question.
   (B)   Said resolution shall be served in the same manner and within the same
time as the initial resolution mentioned in §
111.19 of this code, and insofar as possible, the procedure shall be the same
as is provided in that section.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023)
§ 111.21 PREREQUISITES TO DELIVERY OF LICENSE.
   Retail licenses issued or renewed by the State Liquor Control Commission for
licensees within the village shall be delivered to said licensees by the
Village Clerk, but he or she shall not deliver any such license to a licensee
who does not exhibit receipts showing payment of the occupation tax levied
under §
111.03, payment of the license fee, and payment of the publication fee for
giving notice of the hearing before the Village Board on any application for
license.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023)
§ 111.22 AUTOMATIC RENEWAL NOTICE.
   (A)   The village shall cause to be published in a legal newspaper in or of
general circulation in the village, one time between January 10 and January 30
of each year, individual notice of the right of automatic renewal of each
retail liquor and beer license, except that notice of the right of automatic
renewal for Class C licenses shall be published between the dates of July 10
and July 30 of each year within the village in substantially the following
form:
Notice of Renewal of Retail Liquor License
Notice is hereby given pursuant to Neb. RS 53-135.01 that a liquor license may
be automatically renewed for one year from May 1, 20___, or November 1, 20____,
for the following retail liquor licensee:
________________ __________________________________
(Name of licensee) (Address of licensed premises)
Notice is hereby given that written protests to the issuance of automatic
renewal of license may be filed by any resident of the Village of Petersburg on
or before February 10, 20___, or August 10, 20_____, in the office of the
Village Clerk, and that in the event protests are filed by three or more such
persons, hearing will be had to determine whether continuation of the license
should be allowed.
_______________________________
(Name)
Village Clerk
Village of Petersburg
   (B)   Upon the conclusion of any hearing by this section, the Board of
Trustees may request a licensee to submit an application as provided in Neb. RS
53-135.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023)
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see Neb. RS 53-135.01
§ 111.23 PROTESTS AGAINST RENEWAL.
   (A)   In the event written protests are filed with the Village Clerk by
three or more residents of the village against the automatic renewal of a
license, the Village Clerk shall present the same to the Chairperson and
Village Board at their next meeting, and they shall thereupon by resolution
direct the licensee to submit an application in the same manner as he or she
would be required to do for an original license, and the County Sheriff shall
forthwith serve said resolution upon said licensee by delivering to him or her
personally a true and certified copy thereof.
   (B)   Upon receipt by the Village Clerk from the State Liquor Control
Commission of the notice and copy of application, the same procedure shall be
followed as is provided for in this code in the case of an application for an
original license.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023)
§ 111.24 DISPLAY OF LICENSE.
   Every licensee in this village shall cause his or her license to be framed
and hung in plain view in a conspicuous place on the licensed premises.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023)
RETAIL ESTABLISHMENTS
§ 111.35 SALES FORBIDDEN DURING CERTAIN HOURS.
   (A)   All bars, taverns, and package liquor stores may be open on each
Sunday, if they choose, for on and/or off sale, according to their license
class and in accordance with the provisions of the laws of the state and of the
village.
   (B)   No alcoholic liquors, including beer and wine, may be sold within the
village on any day between the hours of 1:00 a.m. and 6:00 a.m.
   (C)   No alcoholic liquors, including beer and wine, may be sold within the
village on any Sunday except as detailed herein:
      (1)   Sale for on premises consumption:
         (a)   Alcoholic liquor, including beer and wine, shall only be
permitted between the hours of 6:00 a.m. and 1:00 a.m. the following Monday;
and
         (b)   During private events which are not open to the general public,
alcoholic liquor, including beer and wine, shall be permitted between the hours
of 6:00 a.m. and 1:00 a.m. the following Monday.
      (2)   Sale for off premises consumption: alcoholic liquor, including beer
and wine, shall be permitted between the hours of 6:00 a.m. and 1:00 a.m. the
following Monday.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.36 ENTRY OF PREMISES FOR INSPECTION.
   The Village Board of Trustees shall have the power, function, and duty to
enter or to authorize any law enforcement office to enter at any time upon any
premises licensed under the State Liquor Control Act to determine whether any
provision of the act, any rule or regulation adopted and promulgated pursuant
to the act, or any ordinance, resolution, rule, or regulation adopted by the
local Village Board has been or is being violated, and at such time examine the
premises of such licensee in connection with such determination.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023)
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see Neb. RS 53-134(2)
§ 111.37 SALE FOR RESALE.
   No retail licensee in the village shall engage, directly or indirectly, in
any transaction including or conspiring as to the resale of any liquor owned by
him or her as a licensee, nor shall such licensee so permit the sale or
delivery of any such liquors in such quantities as would place a reasonable-
minded person on notice that such liquor might be intended for resale.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.38 TRANSPORTATION OF LIQUOR OF RETAIL LICENSEES.
   No retail licensee in this village shall permit the transportation of
alcoholic liquor from his or her licensed premises for storage purpose in any
manner for any purpose, or to any location other than has been expressly
authorized in writing by the State Liquor Control Commission.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.39 NO DELIVERY AFTER CLOSING HOURS.
   No retail licensee in the village operating a premises open to the public
shall act as retainer or keeper of liquor for customers or other persons for
the purpose of delivering or disposing of such liquor after closing hours as
provided by state law, ordinance, or resolution or on days when sales are
prohibited.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.40 RESTRICTIONS ON CONDUCT OF OTHER BUSINESSES.
   Retail licensees in this village shall not maintain in their licensed
premises any door opening or access leading into the premises owned, used, or
occupied by other persons; nor shall any retail licensee permit any other
person to use his or her licensed premises for the purpose of carrying on,
within such licensed premises, any business activity of such other persons in
any of its phases, such as solicitation, sale, service, delivery, storage, or
otherwise.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.41 CONDUCT PROHIBITED ON LICENSED PREMISES.
   No licensee in this village shall engage in, allow, or suffer in or upon the
licensed premises any disturbance, lewdness, immoral activity or display,
brawl, or unnecessary noise, or allow, permit, or suffer the licensed premises
to be conducted in such a manner as to create public censure or become a
nuisance, public or private.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.42 ADVERTISEMENTS AND SALES.
   Advertising of licensees in the village shall not contain misrepresentation
or misleading statements, and no sales shall be promoted or made by any
licensee by unlawful means. Alcoholic liquors shall not be offered, delivered,
or disposed of by any licensee as a prize.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.43 SANITATION.
   Sanitary conditions, conducive to public health and welfare, must be
maintained at all times, in or about licensed premises in the village.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.44 SALES FOR CASH ONLY.
   No person shall, in the village, sell or furnish alcoholic liquor at retail,
on credit or on a passbook, or order on a store or in exchange for any goods,
wares, or merchandise, or in payment for any services rendered.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.45 PREMISES OPEN TO VIEW.
   Premises licensed for the sale of alcoholic liquor for consumption upon the
premises (other than restaurants, hotels, or clubs) shall have no screen,
blind, curtain, partition, article, or other obstruction in any window or upon
any door of such premises, which shall prevent a clear view into the interior
of such licensed premises from the street, road, or sidewalk at all times, and
shall have no booth, screen, partition, or other obstruction or arrangement of
lights or lighting in or about the interior of such licensed premises which
shall prevent a full view of the entire interior of such licensed premises from
the street, road, or sidewalk. All rooms where liquor is sold for consumption
upon the premises shall be continuously lighted during business hours by
natural or artificial white light so that all parts of the interior of the
premises shall be clearly visible.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any violation of this chapter shall constitute a misdemeanor, any
person convicted of which shall be fined not less than $100 nor more than $500
and assessed the court costs of prosecution.
   (B)   A violation of §
111.15 shall constitute a misdemeanor, any persons convicted of which shall be
fined no less than $100 but no more than $500 and assessed the court costs of
prosecution.
(Ord. 2023-1, passed 9-5-2023)
CHAPTER 112: PEDDLERS AND SOLICITORS
Section
   
112.01   Permits required
   
112.02   Application for permit
   
112.03   Permit conditions
   
112.04   Exhibition of identification
   
112.05   Revocation
   
112.06   Exceptions
 
   
112.99   Penalty
§ 112.01 PERMITS REQUIRED.
   No person shall go in and upon private residences in this village for the
purpose of selling goods, wares, and merchandise or the taking of orders for
the same, without a valid peddler’s permit issued by the Village Clerk.
(Ord. 354, passed 6-2-2009) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 112.02 APPLICATION FOR PERMIT.
   (A)   Peddler’s permits shall be obtained by applying for such with the
Village Clerk. The application shall be substantially the same as follows:
Applicant’s name:______________________________________________________
Applicant’s Social Security number: ______________________________________
Applicant’s address: ___________________________________________________
Applicant’s phone number: ______________________________________________
Company name: _______________________________________________________
Company address: _____________________________________________________
Supervisor’s name: _____________________________________________________
Nature of products/services being sold: _____________________________________
Under penalties of perjury, I state that I have never been convicted of any
crime or ordinance violation except as follows:
______________________________________
State nature of offense, court in which convicted, and approximate date:
__________________________________________________________
References (do not include present employer or any present fellow employee):
Name and address: ________________________________________________
Dated this ______ day of ______, ___________.
Signature of applicant
   (B)   When the application has been properly executed and if the Village
Clerk finds it satisfactory, he or she may issue the permit requested.
(Ord. 354, passed 6-2-2009)
§ 112.03 PERMIT CONDITIONS.
   The Clerk shall issue a permit to each peddler granted one under this
chapter. The permit shall contain the words “Licensed Peddler,” the expiration
date of the permit and the number of the permit. The permit shall be kept with
the peddler during such time as he or she is engaged in the business of
peddling. The permit shall state that it is valid only during the hours of 8:00
a.m. to 8:00 p.m. Monday through Friday.
(Ord. 354, passed 6-2-2009)
§ 112.04 EXHIBITION OF IDENTIFICATION.
   Peddler must present permit to occupant of residence and to police officer
upon request.
(Ord. 354, passed 6-2-2009) Penalty, see §
112.99
§ 112.05 REVOCATION.
   (A)   The permit referred to in §
112.01 shall be valid for one week unless sooner revoked. Such a permit may be
revoked by the Village Clerk after notice and hearing for the following
reasons:
      (1)   Fraud, misrepresentation, or false statement contained in the
application for permit;
      (2)   Fraud, misrepresentation, or false statement made in the course of
carrying on his or her business as a peddler;
      (3)   Conviction of any crime or misdemeanor involving moral turpitude;
      (4)   Conducting the business of peddling in an unlawful manner or in
such a manner as to constitute a breach of the peace or to constitute a menace
to the health, safety, or general welfare of the public; and/or
      (5)   Conducting the business of peddling outside of the hours of 8:00
a.m. to 8:00 p.m., Monday through Friday.
   (B)   Notice of the hearing shall be given in writing, setting forth
specifically the grounds of complaint and the time and place of hearing, which
notice shall be personally served on the permittee by a police officer
designated by the Village Clerk for that purpose at least 24 hours prior to the
time set for hearing, or shall be mailed to the permittee at his or her last
known address at least ten days prior to said time.
(Ord. 354, passed 6-2-2009) Penalty, see §
112.99
§ 112.06 EXCEPTIONS.
   The provisions of §§
112.01 through
112.05 shall not apply to persons selling vegetables, fruit, eggs, poultry,
meat, garden truck, farm products, or provisions produced on their own premises
or charitable organizations previously approved by the Village Board.
(Ord. 354, passed 6-2-2009)
§ 112.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any permittee furnishing false information on or in connection with
his or her application shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor, on conviction
of which he or she shall be fined $150 and assessed the court costs of
prosecution.
   (B)   Any other violation of the provisions of this chapter shall be deemed
a misdemeanor, on conviction of which the offender shall be fined in any sum
not to exceed $200 and assessed the court costs of prosecution.
(Ord. 354, passed 6-2-2009)

130.99   Penalty
OFFENSES AGAINST PUBLIC MORALS AND PEACE
§ 130.01 DRUNKENNESS; NARCOTIC DRUGS; UNDER THE INFLUENCE OF.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to be drunk or under the influence of
intoxicating liquor or under the influence of a narcotic drug, within said
village.
(Ord. 204, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.02 DRINKING ON STREETS OR PUBLIC PROPERTY.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to drink alcoholic liquor of any kind on
the streets or alleys, or upon property used or owned by the United States, the
State of Nebraska, or any governmental subdivision thereof, or in theaters,
dance halls, or in any other place open to or frequented by the public, within
said village.
(Ord. 204, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.03 DISTURBING THE PEACE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to disturb the peace and quiet of any
person, family, neighborhood, or public assembly or to make any loud,
boisterous, or unusual noise, or to quarrel, curse, swear, or use obscene or
indecent language within said village.
(Ord. 204, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.04 DISORDERLY CONDUCT.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in any riotous or disorderly
conduct or fight, strike, or assault another person in a threatening manner, or
to do or engage in any other disorderly act within said village.
(Ord. 204, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.05 VAGRANCY.
   It shall be unlawful for any vagrant to loiter or remain upon the streets,
alleys, or public grounds of said village. A person shall be deemed to be a
VAGRANT who has no visible means of support and lives without employment or
wanders about from place to place begging or receiving alms.
(Ord. 204, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.06 GAMBLING.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to operate or permit to be operated in
said village, any lottery game of chance or gambling except games of chance
which have been authorized by state law and which are operated in accordance
with the license restrictions imposed by state law.
(Ord. 204, passed 10-5-1971; Ord. 363, passed 6-1-2010) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.07 PANDERING, PROSTITUTION, AND ILLICIT SEXUAL INTERCOURSE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in or commit any act of
pandering, prostitution, or illicit sexual intercourse within said village.
(Ord. 204, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.08 HOUSE OF PROSTITUTION; DISORDERLY HOUSE.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to keep, operate, or maintain or
to be an inmate of or visit a house of prostitution or a disorderly house
within said village.
   (B)   A HOUSE OF PROSTITUTION shall be construed to mean a house or other
place which is kept, used, or operated as a place for the commission of acts of
sexual intercourse for hire.
   (C)   A DISORDERLY HOUSE shall be construed to mean any place kept in such a
manner as to disturb, annoy, or scandalize the public generally or persons
within the particular neighborhood, or any place used as a public resort by
drunkards, prostitutes, or other idle or vicious persons or any place of public
resort where illegal practices are habitually carried on to the corruption of
public morals.
(Ord. 204, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.09 MOLESTING.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to molest or force or attempt to force
his or her presence or attention upon any person against his or her desire or
consent in said village.
Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.10 INDECENT EXPOSURE OF PERSON; INDECENT BOOK, PICTURE, PLAY, OR DESIGN.
   It shall be unlawful for any person within said village to make an indecent
exposure of his or her person, or to commit any indecent or lewd act, or to
sell or offer for sale, or to dispose of in any manner any obscene, lewd, or
indecent book, picture, or other publication or thing, or to exhibit or perform
any indecent, immoral, lewd, or obscene play or other representation or in any
public place to write, draw, or make any profane, obscene, indecent, or lewd
work, sentence, figure, or design.
(Ord. 204, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.11 OPEN CONTAINER OF ALCOHOLIC LIQUOR.
   No person shall have in their possession an unsealed, open can, bottle, or
container of alcoholic liquor in a public place, street, or alley or sidewalk,
except a tavern or place where alcoholic liquor is sold, or inside a motor
vehicle while upon any street, alley, or public place in the village.
(Ord. 242, passed 7-5-1978) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.12 DISCHARGE OF DANGEROUS WEAPONS; EXCEPTIONS.
   (A)   Discharge of dangerous weapons. It shall be unlawful for any person to
discharge any firearm, air gun, or slingshot loaded with dangerous missiles
within the village.
   (B)   Exceptions. Division (A) above shall not apply to shooting galleries
or gun safety courses supervised by an adult sponsor who is first approved by
the Chairperson and Village Board of Trustees and is conducted in such a manner
as not to injure or damage any person or property within the village.
Penalty, see §
130.99
OFFENSES AGAINST PROPERTY AND PERSONS
§ 130.25 MALICIOUS DESTRUCTION OF PROPERTY.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, wantonly or maliciously, in any manner,
to molest, injure, or destroy any property of another, in said village.
(Ord. 204, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.26 TRESPASSING.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to remain upon any private or
public property, within said village, without the express permission of the
owner, or party in possession thereof.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person to trespass upon any private
grounds within the village, or to break, cut, or injure any tree, shrub, plant,
flower, or grass growing thereon, or without the consent of the owner or
occupant to enter upon an improved lot or grounds occupied for residence
purposes and to loiter about the same.
(Ord. 204, passed 10-5-1971; Ord. 242, passed 7-5-1978) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.27 WINDOW PEEPING.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to maliciously or stealthily go upon the
premises of another in said village and look or peep into any window, door, or
other opening in any building located thereon which is occupied as a place of
abode, or to go upon the premises of another for the purpose of looking or
peeping into any window, door, or other opening in any building thereon which
is occupied as a place of abode.
(Ord. 204, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.28 RESISTING OR FAILING TO ASSIST AN OFFICER.
   It shall be unlawful for any person in said village to hinder, obstruct, or
resist any police officer or police officer in making any arrest or performing
any duty of his or her office, or to refuse or neglect to assist any such
officer when called upon by him or her in making of any arrest, or the
conveying of a prisoner to jail.
(Ord. 204, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.29 IMPERSONATING AN OFFICER.
   It shall be unlawful for any person in said village other than a regular
police officer or other authorized officer or employee of the village to wear a
badge similar to or resembling the badges prescribed for or furnished the
police force or any other officer or employee of the village, or to willfully
impersonate, or endeavor to impersonate any such police officer or employee or
seek to exercise authority as such.
(Ord. 204, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.30 MOTOR VEHICLE; WRONGFUL TAKING.
   Whoever wrongfully takes any automobile, or motorcycle or other personal
property from a garage, or another place where the same may have been lawfully
placed, without the consent of the owner, or who shall use any motor vehicle in
bailment beyond that use which was originally intended or agreed upon, with
intent to wrongfully use the automobile or motorcycle or other personal
property so taken, shall be guilty of wrongful taking of a motor vehicle,
motorcycle, or other personal property and shall be punished as provided by
law.
(Ord. 242, passed 7-5-1978) Penalty, see §
130.99
CURFEW
§ 130.45 CURFEW HOURS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any minor to loiter, idle, wander, stroll,
play, or be in or upon the public streets, public places and public buildings,
places of amusement and entertainment, vacant lots, or other unsupervised
places, or to ride in or upon, drive, or otherwise operate, any bicycle or
other vehicle, in, upon, over, or through the streets or other public places of
the village between the hours of 11:00 p.m. and 5:00 a.m. on week nights,
Monday through Thursday and between the hours of 12:00 a.m. and 5:00 a.m. of
the following day on the nights of Friday, Saturday, and Sunday.
   (B)   It is an exemption to a violation under this section that the person
engaged in the prohibited conduct while:
      (1)   Accompanied by the minor’s parent or guardian;
      (2)   On an errand at the direction of the minor’s parent or guardian,
without any detour or stop;
      (3)   In a motor vehicle involved in interstate travel;
      (4)   Engaged in an employment activity, or going to or returning home
from an employment activity, without any detour or stop;
      (5)   Involved in an emergency;
      (6)   On the sidewalk abutting the minor’s residence or abutting the
residence of a next-door neighbor if the neighbor did not complain to the
Police Department about the minor’s presence;
      (7)   Attending an official school, religious, or other recreational
activity supervised by adults and sponsored by the city, a civic organization,
or another similar entity that takes responsibility for the minor, or going to
or returning home from, without any detour or stop, an official school,
religious, or other recreational activity supervised by adults and sponsored by
the city, a civic organization, or another similar entity that takes
responsibility for the minor;
      (8)   Exercising First Amendment rights protected by the U.S.
Constitution, such as the free exercise of religion, freedom of speech, and the
right of assembly; or
      (9)   Married or had been married or had disabilities of minority removed
in accordance with state law.
(Ord. 205, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.46 HOURS EXTENDED.
   (A)   Nothing herein contained shall prohibit said minor persons from
attending special school functions or adult supervised entertainment conducted
by any school, church, or fraternal organizations, or adult chaperoned youth
function which shall continue beyond the curfew hours, as set out in §
130.45.
   (B)   In all cases described in division (A) above, the hours herein
prohibited shall be extended for those minors attending said special social
function or entertainment one-half hour after the closing of said special
function.
(Ord. 205, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.47 PARENTAL LIABILITY.
   It shall be unlawful for the parent, guardian, or other adult person, having
the care and custody of a minor under the age of 18 years to allow or permit
said minor persons to do any of the acts or things prohibited by §§
130.45 and
130.46.
(Ord. 205, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.48 ENFORCEMENT; POLICE AUTHORIZATION.
   Every member of the police force while on duty shall be authorized to detain
any such minor willfully violating the provisions of this subchapter, and upon
apprehension of said minor, shall forthwith notify by telephone or other
appropriate means the parents or legal guardians or persons in custody of said
minor child.
(Ord. 205, passed 10-5-1971)
SEXUAL PREDATOR RESIDENCY RESTRICTIONS
§ 130.60 FINDINGS AND INTENT.
   (A)   The State Legislature has found that certain sex offenders present a
high risk to commit repeat offenses and has enabled municipalities to restrict
such persons’ place of residency, as provided in the Sexual Predator Residency
Restriction Act, being Neb. RS 29-4015 et seq.
   (B)   Sex offenders who prey on children and who are high risks to repeat
such acts present an extreme threat to public safety. The cost of sex offender
victimization to these children and to society at large, while incalculable, is
exorbitant.
   (C)   It is the intent of this subchapter to serve the village’s compelling
interest to promote, protect, and improve the health, safety, and welfare of
the citizens of the village by creating certain areas around locations where
children regularly congregate in concentrated numbers where certain sexual
predators cannot reside.
(Ord. 348, passed 8-1-2006)
§ 130.61 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   CHILD CARE FACILITY. A facility licensed pursuant to the Child Care
Licensing Act, being Neb. RS 71-1908 et seq.
   SCHOOL. A public, private, denominational, or parochial school that meets
the requirements for state accreditation or approval.
   RESIDE. To sleep, live, or dwell at a place, which may include more than one
location, and may be mobile or transitory.
   RESIDENCE. A place where an individual sleeps, lives, or dwells, which may
include more than one location, and may be mobile or transitory.
   SEX OFFENDER. An individual who has been convicted of a crime listed in Neb.
RS 29-4003 and who is required to register as a sex offender pursuant to the
Sex Offender Registration Act, being Neb. RS 29-4001 et seq.
   SEXUAL PREDATOR. An individual who is required to register under the Sex
Offender Registration Act, being Neb. RS 29-4001 et seq., who has been
classified as Level 3 because of a high risk of recidivism as determined by the
State Patrol under Neb. RS 29-4013, and who has victimized a person 18 years of
age or younger.
(Ord. 348, passed 8-1-2006)
§ 130.62 RESTRICTIONS; EXCEPTIONS.
   (A)   Prohibited location of residence. It is unlawful for any sexual
predator to reside within 500 feet from a school or child care facility.
   (B)   Measure of distance. For purposes of determining the minimum distance
separation, the distance shall be measured by following a straight line from
the outer property line of the residence to the nearest outer boundary line of
the school or child care facility.
   (C)   Exceptions. This subchapter shall not apply to a sexual predator who:
      (1)   Resides within a prison or correctional or treatment facility
operated by the state or a political subdivision;
      (2)   Established a residence before July 1, 2006, and has not moved from
that residence; or
      (3)   Established a residence after July 1, 2006, and the school or child
care facility triggering the restriction was established after the initial date
of the sexual predator’s residence at that location.
(Ord. 348, passed 8-1-2006) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Any person violating any of the provision of §§
130.01 through
130.11 and
130.25 through
130.29 upon conviction shall be fined not more than $100 and pay the cost of
prosecution.
   (C)   Any person who shall violate or refuse to comply with the enforcement
of any of the provisions of §
130.30 shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor, and upon conviction thereof,
shall be fined not more than $100 for each offense. A new violation shall be
deemed to have been committed every 24 hours of such failure to comply.
   (D)   Any violation of the provisions of §§
130.45 through
130.48 shall constitute a misdemeanor, and shall be punishable by a fine of $50
for the first offense, $100 for the second offense and subsequent offenses, and
shall be assessed the court costs of prosecution.
   (E)   Anyone violating any of the terms or conditions of §§
130.60 through
130.62 shall be punished by a fine not more than $500 for each offense. Each
day’s maintenance of the same shall constitute a separate offense. The village
may bring an appropriate action or proceedings to prevent the continuing
violation of §§
130.60 through
130.62, or to abate such violation.
(Ord. 204, passed 10-5-1971; Ord. 205, passed 10-5-1971; Ord. 242, passed 7-5-
1978; Ord. 348, passed 8-1-2006)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 150.01 REGISTRATION OF VACANT PROPERTY.
   (A)   For the purpose of this section, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
      COMMERCIAL BUILDING. Any building used for commercial purposes. Examples
of COMMERCIAL BUILDINGS include, but are not limited to, offices, retail
spaces, warehouses, and factories.
      OWNER. The person or persons shown to be the owner or owners of record on
the records of the register of deeds.
      PROGRAM ADMINISTRATOR. The Village Health Board.
      PROPERTY. Either a residential building or a commercial building located
within the corporate limits of the village but does not include property owned
by the federal government, the state, or any political subdivision thereof.
      RESIDENTIAL BUILDING. A house, a condominium, a townhouse, an apartment
unit, or building, a trailer house, or any other structure used or designed for
use as a residence.
      VACANT. A property is VACANT if any condition or circumstance that on its
own, or in combination with other conditions or circumstances, would lead a
reasonable person to believe that the property is VACANT. Such conditions or
circumstances may include, but are not limited to:
         (a)   Overgrown or dead vegetation, including grass, shrubbery, and
other plantings;
         (b)   An accumulation of abandoned personal property, trash, or other
waste;
         (c)   Visible deterioration or lack of maintenance of any building or
structure on the property;
         (d)   Graffiti or other defacement of any building or structure on the
property; or
         (e)   Any other condition or circumstance reasonably indicating that
the property is not occupied for residential purposes or being used for the
operation of a lawful business.
   (B)   The owner of a vacant property must register such property with the
program administrator if the property has been vacant for 180 days or longer.
At the time of registration, the owner must submit a plan for occupancy for the
property detailing how and when the property will be occupied or used.
   (C)   A vacant property registration ordinance registration form shall be in
either paper or electronic form, and the following information shall be
required:
      (1)   The name, street address, mailing address, telephone number, and,
if applicable, the facsimile number and email address of the property owner and
his or her agent;
      (2)   The street address and parcel identification number of the vacant
property;
      (3)   The transfer date of the instrument conveying the property to the
owner; and
      (4)   The date on which the property became vacant.
   (D)   The program administrator may, but is not obligated to, determine a
property is vacant. The program administrator will provide written notice to
the owner of any such determination by certified mail to the owner at the
address maintained in the register of deeds’ office at least ten days prior to
such a determination.
   (E)   One-hundred eighty days after the initial registration of a vacant
property, or 360 days after the property becomes vacant, whichever is earlier,
the owner must pay a fee of $250 for a residential building or $1,000 for a
commercial building.
   (F)   Every six months following the assessment of the initial registration
fee, the owner of a vacant property must pay a supplemental registration fee of
$500 for a residential building or $2,000 for a commercial building as long as
the property remains vacant. The total supplemental registration fee may not
exceed ten times the initial registration fee amount.
   (G)   An owner who, in good faith, advertises a vacant property for sale or
lease is exempt from the above registration and fee requirements.
   (H)   The following exemptions apply to the vacant property registration and
fee requirements:
      (1)   A residential building used only as seasonal residence is exempt
provided the building is seasonally occupied;
      (2)   A property damaged by fire, weather, explosion, act of God, or
vandalism within six months prior to becoming vacant is exempt from the
requirements. Such damaged properties are no longer exempt after the six-month
period;
      (3)   A property under construction or renovation is exempt to the extent
the construction or renovation is ongoing and in compliance with all relevant
building permits and codes;
      (4)   A residential building where the owner is temporarily absent, but
who has demonstrated his or her intent to return is exempt unless it is
subsequently determined the owner does not intend to return; and
      (5)   A property which is subject to divorce, probate, or estate
proceedings is exempt until the end of the respective proceeding.
   (I)   Any subsequent owner of a vacant property subject to this section
assumes the obligations of the previous owner.
   (J)   The program administrator may annually inspect the interior and
exterior of a registered vacant property so long as the property remains on the
vacant property registration database. An owner will be provided at least ten
days’ notice prior to an annual inspection.
   (K)   Upon written notice from the owner of a registered vacant property to
the program administrator that the property is no longer vacant, the program
administrator will within 30 days inspect the interior and exterior of the
property to confirm the property is no longer vacant. The owner must pay any
supplemental registration fee that comes due during the period between the
owner’s written notice and the program administrator’s inspection, but upon the
program administrator’s confirmation the property is no longer vacant, the
program administrator may refund the supplemental registration fee so
occurring.
   (L)   After the program administrator confirms a property is no longer
vacant, the program administrator will remove the property from the vacant
property registration database within seven days. No supplemental registration
fee will be assessed after confirmation that a property is no longer vacant
irrespective of the property’s presence on the registration database.
   (M)   Owners have the right to prior notice and to appeal adverse decisions
of the program administrator to the Village Board of Trustees. Such appeal
shall be taken by filing with the Village Board of Trustees, within seven days
after a notice of the decision has been mailed to the owner’s last known
address, a written statement setting for the grounds for the appeal. The
Village Board of Trustees shall set the time and place for a hearing on such
appeal, and notice shall be given to the owner by certified or registered mail,
postage prepaid, at the owner’s last known address. The order of the Village
Board of Trustees on such appeal shall be final.
   (N)   Failure to comply with the requirements of this section is a violation
of this section, and is subject to the penalties found in §
150.99.
   (O)   The requirements and remedies in this section are supplemental and in
addition to any other laws of the state and the provisions of this code
relating to vacant property.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 2-4-2020) Penalty, see §
150.99
UNSAFE STRUCTURES
§ 150.15 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definition shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   UNSAFE STRUCTURE. 
      (1)   Any building, shed, fence, or other human-made structure which:
         (a)   Is dangerous to the public health because of its condition, and
which may cause or aid in the spread of disease or injury to the health of the
occupants or neighboring structures;
         (b)   Because of faulty construction, age, lack of proper repair, or
any other cause is especially susceptible to fire, creating a fire hazard; or
         (c)   By reason of faulty construction or any other cause is liable to
cause injury or damage by the collapse or fall of all or any part of such
structure.
      (2)   Any such unsafe structure within the municipal limits of the
village is hereby declared to be a nuisance.
(Ord. 293-2014, passed 7-1-2014)
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see Neb. RS 18-1720 and 18-1722
§ 150.16 PROHIBITION.
   It shall be unlawful to maintain or permit the existence of any unsafe
structure within the municipal limits of the village and it shall be unlawful
for the owner, occupant, or person in custody of any unsafe structure to permit
the same to remain in an unsafe condition or to occupy such structure or permit
it to be occupied while it is in an unsafe condition.
(Ord. 293-2014, passed 7-1-2014) Penalty, see §
150.99
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see Neb. RS 18-1720 and 18-1722
§ 150.17 DETERMINATION AND NOTICE.
   (A)   Whenever the Health Board and or the Village Board of Trustees shall
be of the opinion that any structure in the municipal limits of the village is
an unsafe structure, it shall file a written statement to this effect with the
Village Clerk.
   (B)   The Clerk shall serve written notice upon the owner thereof, and upon
the occupant thereof, if any, by certified mail or by personal service. Such
notice shall state that the structure has been declared to be in an unsafe
condition; and that such unsafe condition must be removed or remedied within 60
days from the date of receipt. Such notice shall include the name or the owner
or occupant of the premises, the location of the premises, a description of the
structure found to be unsafe, and conditions giving rise to the determination.
Such notice shall also include the possible consequences of noncompliance and
the owner or occupant’s rights to an appeal.
(Ord. 293-2014, passed 7-1-2014)
§ 150.18 HEARING AND APPEAL.
   (A)   Upon receiving notice to remedy the unsafe structure, the noticed
party, within the time stipulated, may make a written request to the Village
Clerk for a hearing before the Village Board of Trustees, to present reasons
why the building should not be repaired or demolished.
   (B)   The Board of Trustees shall grant such a hearing within ten days of
receipt of the request for a hearing.
   (C)   The Board of Trustees shall issue a written notice of their decision
following the hearing by certified mail to the requesting party. If the appeal
is rejected, the noticed party shall have 60 days from receipt of the finding
in order to remove or remedy the unsafe structure.
   (D)   If the unsafe structure has not been remedied or removed within this
time, the village shall have the right to enter onto the property and
accomplish such work as is necessary to remedy or remove the unsafe structure
and levy the costs of such work against the property; provided, the noticed
party(ies) may appeal such decision to the County Court for adjudication,
during which proceedings the decision of the Board of Trustees shall be stayed.
(Ord. 293-2014, passed 7-1-2014)
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see Neb. RS 18-1720 and 18-1722
§ 150.19 EMERGENCY.
   Where any unsafe structure poses an immediate danger to the health, safety,
or general welfare of any person or persons, and the owner fails to remedy the
situation in a reasonable time after notice by the Health Board and/or Board of
Trustees to do so, the village may summarily repair or demolish and remove such
building or structure.
(Ord. 293-2014, passed 7-1-2014)
§ 150.20 SPECIAL ASSESSMENTS.
   (A)   If any owner or any structure fails, neglects, or refuses to comply
with notice by or on behalf of the village to repair, rehabilitate, or demolish
and remove a structure which is unsafe and a public nuisance, the village may
proceed with the work specified as set out above. A statement of the cost of
such work shall be transmitted to the Board of Trustees.
   (B)   The Board of Trustees may:
      (1)   Levy the cost as a special assessment against the real estate upon
which the structure is located, and such special assessment shall be a lien on
the real estate and shall be collected in the manner provided for special
assessments; or
      (2)   Collect the cost from the owner of the structure and enforce the
collection by civil action in any court of competent jurisdiction.
(Ord. 293-2014, passed 7-1-2014)
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see Neb. RS 18-1720 and 18-1722
ERECTING, REMODELING, AND MOVING OF BUILDINGS
§ 150.35 PERMIT AND BOND REQUIRED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to move any building over or across any
street or public way of the village until a permit therefor has been issued by
the Street Commissioner, and all other provisions of this subchapter complied
with. The Street Commissioner, is hereby authorized to issue such permit upon
the written permission or application of the owner of said building proposed to
be removed, or of his or her agent, showing the size and kind of building, its
then location and its proposed location; but said permit shall not be issued
until the owner of said building shall be bond with good and sufficient surety
in such sum as the Street Commissioner shall fix and determine, said bond to be
conditioned among other things that said licensee will in all things strictly
comply with all the provisions of the ordinances of the village relating to
house-moving and that said licensee will save, indemnify, and keep harmless the
said village from all liabilities judgments, costs, and expenses which may in
anywise accrue against it in consequence of the granting of such license and
that said licensee will pay to said village and all damages which may be
sustained by any pavement, curb, gutter, sidewalk, street, or other village
property through the moving of such building by said licensee, and that said
licensee shall pay the owner any and all damage caused in a like manner to any
private property in said village. Said bond shall be approved in writing by the
Street Commissioner before such license is issued. The Street Commissioner in
said permit shall limit the time of removal and shall specify the route to be
followed in moving said building over and across the streets and public ways of
said village, and it shall be unlawful for any such licensee to digress from
such time or specified route without permission or written consent of the
Street Commissioner. In prescribing the route to be followed, the Street
Commissioner shall prescribe such route as will least interfere with telephone
systems and lighting systems in said village under all circumstances.
(Ord. 214, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.36 NOTICE TO PUBLIC SERVICE COMPANIES REQUIRED.
   Before moving any building, the licensee shall notify all public service
companies whose wires or other appliances may obstruct the moving of such
building of the time when such building will be moved, and request such public
service companies to arrange for the passage of such building, and such
licensee shall pay said public service companies the reasonable and actual cost
and expense of the work required to be done.
(Ord. 214, passed 10-5-1971)
§ 150.37 CARE REQUIRED OF LICENSEE.
   It shall be unlawful for any licensee to make any openings or excavations in
any street pavement or to set any stakes therein, and it is hereby made a duty
of every licensee to move any such buildings so moved by him or her in a
careful manner and with the least possible injury to the public or private
property, and for every such injury or damage, he or she shall be liable on his
or her bond. The Street Commissioner’s estimate of any damage done to village
property by any licensee shall be final and conclusive upon said licensee.
(Ord. 214, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.38 BUILDING PERMITS; PROCEDURE TO OBTAIN.
   (A)   Any person desiring to construct, reconstruct, or otherwise change the
contour or size of any building or other structure, shall, before so doing,
file a written application with the Village Clerk for a permit therefor,
setting out the type of building or other structure, the legal description of
the lot or parcel of land upon which it is to be located, and where it is now
located if within said village, the part or portion of the lot or parcel of
land to be occupied by said building or other structure, the probable cost of
the building or improvement, or the value of the building or improvement, or
the type of construction of all chimneys, smokestacks, and flues and any
additional plans or specifications or details that may be required by the
Village Board.
   (B)   No work shall be done in connection with said project until a permit
therefor shall have been granted and issued in accordance with the provisions
of this subchapter.
(Ord. 222, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.39 ACTION BY BOARD.
   It shall be the duty of the Village Clerk to refer all such applications to
the Chairperson and Board at the first regular or special meeting after the
same shall have been filed, and the Board may at all times determine whether or
not a permit shall be granted, or may continue the matter to a later date for
hearing, upon such notice as the Board shall prescribe.
(Ord. 222, passed 10-5-1971)
§ 150.40 ISSUANCE OF PERMIT.
   If it is determined by the Village Board that a permit should be granted,
the Village Clerk shall forthwith issue such permit granting the request of the
applicant in accordance with the details set out in the application or
specifying in detail any changes in construction or otherwise that have been
prescribed by the Village Board and all work shall be done strictly in
accordance with the terms of the permit.
(Ord. 222, passed 10-5-1971)
§ 150.41 BUILDING WITHOUT PERMIT; NUISANCE.
   Every building or other structure hereafter erected, remodeled, or moved
into or within said village without a permit therefor as herein required, or
which is not constructed, remodeled, or located in accordance with the permit
granted and issued therefor, shall be deemed and considered to be a public
nuisance and may be abated or removed by the village at the expense of the
owner.
(Ord. 222, passed 10-5-1971)
§ 150.42 UNFINISHED AND UNSAFE BUILDINGS.
   No building or other structure in said village shall be allowed to remain in
an unfinished condition for a period of over six months, nor shall any building
or other structure in said village be allowed to remain in an unsafe, damaged,
or demolished condition for a period of more than 60 days.
(Ord. 222, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.43 OFFENSIVE USES.
   No building or premises in said village shall be used for any trade,
industry, or purpose that is obnoxious or offensive by reason of the emission
of odor, dust, smoke, gas fumes, or noise, or that is otherwise detrimental to
the health, safety, or general welfare of the community.
(Ord. 222, passed 10-5-1971) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Any person who shall violate or refuse to comply with the enforcement
of any of the provisions of §§
150.15 through
150.20 set forth herein or incorporated by reference shall be deemed guilty of
a misdemeanor, and upon conviction thereof, shall be fined not less than $100
nor more than $500 for each offense. A new violation of §§
150.15 through
150.20 shall be deemed to have been committed every 24 hours of such failure to
comply.
   (C)   Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of §§
150.35 through
150.37 upon conviction shall be fined in any sum not more than $100 and shall
pay the costs of prosecution.
   (D)   Every person who violates any of the provisions of §§
150.38 through
150.43 upon conviction shall be fined not more than $100 and shall pay the
costs of prosecution, and each day that a violation continues shall be a
separate offense.
(Ord. 214, passed 10-5-1971; Ord. 222, passed 10-5-1971; Ord. 293-2014, passed
7-1-2014)
CHAPTER 151: ZONING

151.01   Zoning Code; adopted by reference
§ 151.01 ZONING CODE; ADOPTED BY REFERENCE.
   The Village Board of Trustees adopts and incorporates the Zoning and
Subdivision Ordinance for the village, including the zoning jurisdiction
extending one-mile from the corporate limits of the village, as recommended by
the County Joint Planning Commission after the completion of the required
public hearing.

   Table
